                                          Board of Education Agenda
                                               March 25, 2025


                                PUBLIC PARTICIPATION GUIDELINES
Board of Education meetings are held in person in the board room located at 3738 Walnut Avenue, Carmichael,
California. Alternatively, you can view the board meeting virtually via livestream from a computer, mobile device
or tablet at https://www.sanjuan.edu/boardmeeting. The district has taken the following steps to assist the public in
offering public comment:

     1. In Person Public Comment. Public comment may be offered in person during the board meeting at the
        district office located at 3738 Walnut Avenue, Carmichael, California. Board Bylaw 9323 limits visitor
        comments to two (2) minutes per speaker, with no more than 30 minutes per single topic. Time will be
        extended for any speaker who uses an interpreter. Please be aware that public comments, including your
        name, become part of the public record.
     2. Online Submission of Public Comment. Members of the public may submit written comments by using the
        comment form located on the district website at http://www.sanjuan.edu/boardmeeting. If you wish to
        submit a written comment on more than one agenda item, please submit a separate form for each item on
        which you are commenting. Written comments are limited to 1,500 characters. Comments will be provided
        to the members of the board.

A.    OPEN SESSION/CALL TO ORDER/ANNOUNCEMENT OF CLOSED SESSION TOPICS - 5:15
      p.m.
      1. Visitor Comments (for closed session agenda items only)
      Board Bylaw 9323 limits visitor comments to two (2) minutes per speaker, with no more than 30 minutes per
      single topic. Time will be extended for any speaker who uses an interpreter. Public comments, including your
      name, become part of the public record.

        1. Student expulsion in one case (Education Code section 48918[f]).

                                  NOTE: The times indicated are approximate.
The Board of Education welcomes and encourages the public’s participation at the board meetings and has devoted
time throughout the meeting for that purpose. You may comment on items included on this agenda; however, we
ask that you limit your comments to two (2) minutes, so that as many people as possible may be heard (Education
Code section 35145.5, Government Code section 54954.3).

A person with a disability may contact the Board of Education office at (916) 971-7111, or email
stephanie.cunningham@sanjuan.edu at least 48 hours before the scheduled board meeting to request receipt of an
agenda and other distributed writings in an appropriate alternative format, or to request disability-related
modifications or accommodations, including auxiliary aids or services, in order to participate in the public board
meeting.

Translation and interpretation services will be made available upon request with advance notice. If you wish to
utilize these services, please notify the Board of Education office at (916) 971-7111, or email
stephanie.cunningham@sanjuan.edu at least 24 hours before the scheduled board meeting to allow for the
scheduling of appropriate translation staff and other resources.

                                                Mission Statement
We partner with our San Juan Unified community in setting high expectations for academic achievement rooted in
equity and unity to create supportive learning experiences in which all students, families and staff can excel and
thrive.

                               San Juan Unified Land Acknowledgement
The San Juan Unified School District acknowledges that our schools are located on the ancestral lands of the
Nisenan and Miwok peoples, who continue to care for this land as they have since time immemorial. We deeply



                                                                                                                     4
respect their ongoing connection to this land and recognize their resilience in preserving and revitalizing their
cultures and traditions despite historical and ongoing challenges.

We recognize the profound injustices endured by their ancestors, including genocide, forced assimilation, and
displacement, and we remain aware of the ongoing challenges and injustices they face today. As we advance in our
commitment to equity and inclusion, we pledge to strengthen our connections by fostering a culture of
understanding, respect, and active collaboration with their communities.

                                              Board of Education Minutes
                                                   March 11, 2025

Regular Meeting
Board of Education
5:45 p.m.

Open Session/Call to Order (A)
The March 11 regular meeting was called to order by the president, Ben Avey. The board meeting was held in person and
was also livestreamed on the district website.

Roll Call
Present:
Ben Avey, president
Tanya Kravchuk, vice president
Manuel Perez, clerk
Zima Creason, member
Nick Bloise, member
Abid Stanekzai, member
Pam Costa, member

Announcement of Closed Session Topics/Closed Session Visitor Comments (A-1)
There were no closed session visitor comments.

Closed Session (B)
The meeting was then recessed with the board convening in closed session to discuss one personnel matter – one
reassignment of a certificated administrator (Government Code section 54957); and to conference with legal counsel –
anticipated litigation: significant exposure to litigation (Government Code section 54956.9(d)(2) and (4)).

Reconvene Open Session/Pledge of Allegiance (C)
At 6:30 p.m., the March 11 regular meeting was called back to order by the president, Ben Avey. Four members of the Casa
Roble Fundamental High School Jr. ROTC led the group in the Pledge of Allegiance.

Minutes Approved (D)
It was moved by Mr. Bloise, seconded by Mr. Perez, that the minutes of the February 25 regular meeting be approved.
MOTION CARRIED 5-0-2 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Bloise, Stanekzai; NOES: None; ABSTAIN: Creason, Costa].

High School Student Council Reports (E-1)
High School Student Council representatives Emi Kuwabara from El Camino Fundamental High School and Lucas Firl and
Georgia Klostrakis from Mira Loma High School updated the board on the goals, activities and achievements at their
respective schools.

Board-appointed/District Committees (E-3)
Frank Cockrell, chair of the Facilities Committee, provided an update on the work of the committee.

Closed Session/Expulsion Actions (E-6)
Mr. Perez reported that the board voted 5-0 with 2 abstentions to reassign one certificated administrator.

                                                                                                                   2664
                                                                                                                           7
Budget Financial Status Report/2024-2025 Second Interim Report (I-1)
Chief Financial Officer Joel Ryan presented the 2024-2025 Second Interim Report, certifying the Second Interim Report
as positive, with the understanding of the fiduciary responsibility to maintain fiscal solvency for the current and subsequent
two fiscal years. The Second Interim Report reflects actual revenue and expenditures through January 31, 2025, forecasts
the remainder of the 2024-2025 fiscal year, and provides a multi-year budget projection for years 2025-2026 and 2026-
2027.

It was moved by Mr. Bloise, seconded by Ms. Costa, to approve the 2024-2025 Second Interim Report with the positive
certification of the district’s ability to meet its financial obligations for the current fiscal year and subsequent two fiscal
years. MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise, Costa; NOES: None; ABSTAIN:
Stanekzai].

Measure P (2016) and Measure P (2024) Update (I-2)
Mr. Ryan presented the topic and introduced Isom Advisors Principal Jason List and Raymond James Financial Inc.
Managing Director Brett Lee who gave a tax rate presentation on Measure P (2016) and Measure P (2024). Mr. List and
Mr. Lee discussed the district’s tax base, historical assessed values, Measure P plan of finance, tax rate estimates and
historical and projected tax rates as well as a timeline of steps to a potential bond sale later this year. Board members
thanked the bond team for their efforts and made comments regarding fiscal responsibility.

Facilities Master Plan (I-3)
Chief Operations Officer Frank Camarda introduced the item and thanked the team, explaining that the updated Facilities
Master Plan serves as a long-term roadmap and vision for the district’s facility needs. Mr. Camarda discussed the extensive
community outreach that took place. Derek Labrecque from JKAE Design shared that the plan includes comprehensive
assessments of the physical conditions and educational environments, as well as cost analyses of each campus and support
sites. Mr. Labrecque further explained that the plan incorporates educational goals, updated site and building plan concepts,
useful life data of major building systems, demographic analysis, state funding opportunities, capacity, utilization, deferred
maintenance and a scoring rubric to assist in making data-driven decisions for project implementation. Mr. Camarda also
reviewed some of the additional project implementation planning factors that may need to be considered, such as state
mandates, security initiatives, evolving demographics, educational programs, large capital assets, compliance issues or
emergencies. Jason Villanueva from VM3 Consulting and Cherie Chenoweth, San Juan Unified Facilities Business and
Compliance Coordinator, demonstrated the interactive website and public-facing dashboard, explaining that the platform
will support proactive planning for project development and show updates as projects progress. Mr. Camarda explained
next steps, which includes the completion of the master plan and the launch of the public-facing interactive tool in June
2025.

Board members expressed support for the plan and posed questions, which staff addressed. Ms. Creason spoke about the
Facilities Committee, the connection to LCAP actions, the community engagement process, the rollout process and
variables that may impact project priority recommendations. Ms. Kravchuk expressed appreciation for the transparency and
interactive nature of the dashboard, and she inquired about the visibility of historical updates and the rubric. Mr. Bloise
inquired if principals had seen the vision plans. Mr. Avey shared that he believes the rubric will dictate which projects need
to be prioritized 95 percent of the time; however, he proposed adding language to the motion to allow the superintendent
flexibility in addressing the remaining 5 percent. There was general consensus among board members to add the language.

It was moved by Ms. Creason, seconded by Mr. Perez, to approve the Facilities Master Plan rubric for future project
development and implementation while authorizing the superintendent to modify the plan to meet district needs. MOTION
CARRIED UNANIMOUSLY [Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise, Stanekzai, Costa].

Resolution Reducing or Discontinuing Particular Kinds of Services - TK-12 Certificated (I-4)
Chief of Human Resources Rebecca Toto, Ed.D., presented the item.

Public Comments:

Anna Romeo spoke about the work of school counselors and reasonable caseloads.

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                  AGENDA ITEM:                   E.1
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                  MEETING DATE:               03/25/2025

SUBJECT: Week of the Young Child

DEPARTMENT: Teaching and Learning

ACTION REQUESTED:
Action: The superintendent is recommending that the board adopt Resolution No. A-449, proclaiming the week of
April 5-11, 2025, as the Week of the Young Child.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The Week of the Young Child is formally recognized by early childhood education professionals throughout the
United States each year in April. In support of this nationally recognized event, the San Juan Unified School
District’s Early Childhood Education Department involves school staff, students and community members in
celebrating the Week of the Young Child.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. Resolution No. A-449 Week of the Young Child

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A

PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 03/17/2025

FISCAL IMPACT:
N/A

PREPARED BY:                Lisa Teal, Program Manager, Early Childhood Education

APPROVED BY:                Amberlee Townsend-Snider, Asst. Superintendent, Elementary Education & Programs
                            Amy L. Slavensky, Ph.D., Interim Deputy Superintendent, Schools & Student Support
                            Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools




                                                                                                                10
                          SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT
                                 Resolution No. A-449

                                WEEK OF THE YOUNG CHILD
                                     April 5-11, 2025


WHEREAS, the San Juan Unified School District has a commitment to encourage and support
learning beginning at birth and continuing throughout a person's life; and

WHEREAS, April 5-11, 2025, is being recognized as Week of the Young Child throughout the United
States; and

WHEREAS, the Early Childhood Education Department has primary responsibility for providing
quality educational, social, and emotional services to meet the diverse needs of thousands of
families and children in the infant/toddler, preschool and before and after school programs; and

WHEREAS, thousands of parents and caregivers receive their first family education and family
involvement experiences through the Early Childhood Education Department; and

WHEREAS, hundreds of children receive mental and physical health follow-up through the Early
Childhood Education Department; and

WHEREAS, other departments and programs such as Birth and Beyond, Adult Education, Special
Education, Student Assistance and Prevention Programs and P-6 teachers, counselors, nurses and
administrators serve as partners with the Early Childhood Education Department;

NOW THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED by the San Juan Unified School District Board of Education,
that it recognizes the week of April 5-11, 2025, as Week of the Young Child in honor of the outstanding
services provided by Early Childhood Education staff members in the San Juan Unified School
District; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that the district commends San Juan Unified’s Early Childhood
Education administrators, teachers and other staff members for their significant contributions to the
education of infants, toddlers, preschoolers, and young children in our community.

Attested to this 25th day of March 2025                ________________________________
                                                       Ben Avey, President

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                      AGENDA ITEM:                     E.2
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                      MEETING DATE:                03/25/2025

SUBJECT: School Library Month

DEPARTMENT: Teaching and Learning

ACTION REQUESTED:
Action: The superintendent is recommending that the board adopt Resolution No. A-450, recognizing the month of
April as School Library Month.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The resolution recognizes the month of April as School Library Month, in partnership with the American
Association of School Librarians, and acknowledges continued district support for the school libraries and the staff
who support them, including our teacher librarians. San Juan Unified School District believes that a well-rounded
education includes access to school libraries which fosters critical thinking, self-expression, lifelong learning
skills, and readiness for college and career.
ATTACHMENT(S):
1. Resolution No. A-450 School Library Month

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A

PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 03/17/2025

FISCAL IMPACT:
N/A

                             Nicole Kukral, Director, Professional Learning and Curriculum Innovation

APPROVED BY:                 Amy Slavensky, Ph.D., Interim Deputy Superintendent, Schools and Student Support
                             Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools




                                                                                                                       12
                                    SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT
                                            Resolution No. A-450

                                                  School Library Month
                                                       April, 2025

WHEREAS, we strongly believe that teacher librarians are an essential part of a well-rounded education from preschool
through grade 12; and

WHEREAS, through their expertise in information literacy, digital citizenship, and fostering a love of reading, teacher
librarians help students develop critical thinking, problem-solving, communication, collaboration, self-expression, and
lifelong learning skills; and

WHEREAS, classified school library staff play a vital role in supporting elementary and middle school students by
creating welcoming spaces that foster a love of reading, with their hard work keeping school libraries running smoothly,
providing essential support to students and staff;

WHEREAS, the Every Student Succeeds Act (ESSA) fully supports a “well-rounded education” with the goal of fully
preparing all students for success in college and careers; and

WHEREAS, research has demonstrated that school libraries and teacher librarians contribute to higher academic
achievement, improved reading scores, and increased student engagement; and

WHEREAS, thousands of students in San Juan Unified benefit from the resources and support provided by our
dedicated teacher librarians in the classroom and in the library; and

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED that the Board of Education proposes continued support of teacher
librarians and classified library staff. This resolution gives recognition to the students in our district and our dedicated
teacher librarians and classified library staff.

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED that the Board of Education applauds the demonstrated enthusiasm and dedication of
the San Juan Unified teacher librarians and classified library staff who inspire a love of reading, support academic
achievement, and foster a culture of inquiry and learning in our schools and in our community.

Attested to this 25th day of March 2025                     ________________________________
                                                            Ben Avey, President

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                    AGENDA ITEM:                    E.3
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                    MEETING DATE:               03/25/2025

SUBJECT: Adult Education Week

DEPARTMENT: Teaching and Learning

ACTION REQUESTED:
Action: The superintendent is recommending that the board adopt Resolution No. A-451, recognizing the week of
April 6-12, 2025, as Adult Education Week.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
San Juan Unified School District commits to encourage and support lifelong learning and meet the diverse needs of
our community's adult and high school students. Adult education teachers incorporate a rich variety of evidence-
based practices which support multiple learning styles and promote student achievement. In recognition of San
Juan Unified's Adult Education Program, the district proclaims the week of April 6-12, 2025, as Adult Education
Week. This resolution is in appreciation for the outstanding services provided to the adults in our community by
the dedicated and caring employees and volunteers of the Adult Education program.
ATTACHMENT(S):
1. Resolution No. A-451 Adult Education Week

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
NA

PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 03/17/2025

FISCAL IMPACT:
NA

PREPARED BY:                Kristan Schnepp, Assistant Superintendent, Secondary Education and Programs

APPROVED BY:                Amy L. Slavensky, Ph.D., Interim Deputy Superintendent, Schools & Student Services
                            Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools




                                                                                                                    14
                                    SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT
                                           Resolution No. A-451

                                              Adult Education Week
                                                April 6-12, 2025


WHEREAS, Adult Education Week is April 6-12, 2025; and

WHEREAS, the first recorded adult education class in California was held in the basement of St. Mary’s Cathedral
in San Francisco in 1856. The San Francisco Board of Education authorized the class to teach English as a second
language to Irish, Italian, and Chinese immigrants. John Swett, who was the first volunteer teacher for the class,
later became a State Superintendent of Public Instruction; and

WHEREAS, adult education schools have been utilized on numerous occasions to assist the state as it dealt with
significant social, political and economic issues through job training programs during World War II, immigration
reform of the 1980s and the Great Recession; and

WHEREAS, adult education in California overcame its biggest challenges as a result of the severe economic crisis
facing both the state and the nation in 2008-2009 as funding that was reserved for adult education was redistributed
to other levels of education; and

WHEREAS, San Juan Unified Adult Education successfully serves the surrounding communities through its
collaboration with its community college partners and community-based organizations through the Adult Education
system, and

WHEREAS, San Juan Unified Adult Education provides significant and varied classes and programs to serve the
surrounding communities including courses in healthcare training, computer technologies training, job preparation
classes, high school diploma and equivalency programs, English as a second language (ESL) classes, citizenship
classes and more; and

THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED that the board and superintendent strongly support Adult Education Week and
acknowledge April 6-12, 2025, as California Adult Education Week.

Attested to this 25th day of March 2025               ________________________________
                                                      Ben Avey, President

SUBJECT: Surplus Property

DEPARTMENT: Fiscal Services

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the disposal of surplus property pursuant to Board
Policy 3270.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The Governing Board recognizes that the district may own personal property, which is unusable, obsolete, or no
longer needed by the district. The superintendent or designee shall arrange for the sale or disposal of district
personal property in accordance with board policy and the requirements or state law.

The superintendent or designee shall identify to the board all items not needed by the district together with their
estimated value and a recommended disposition.

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                      AGENDA ITEM:                     H.6
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                      MEETING DATE:                 03/25/2025

SUBJECT: Head Start (HS) and Early Head Start (EHS) Grant Application 2025-2026

DEPARTMENT: Teaching and Learning

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the submission and implementation of, if funded, the
Head Start and Early Head Start Grant 2025-2026.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The annual Head Start and Early Head Start grant application seeks to renew funding for the 2025-26 fiscal year.
These programs provide comprehensive services for pregnant women and children from infancy to age five,
supporting education, health, mental health, career development, adult education, and access to community
resources. These programs play a crucial role in supporting early childhood development and ensure children are
prepared for academic success at young ages.

Student enrollment in the Head Start preschool program is shifting focus toward younger students (three year olds)
who require greater support in developing self-care routines, which equates to a requirement and need for lower
student to adult ratios.

To accomplish this, and as a part of this grant renewal, we will continue to receive funding for 72 student seats in
the Head Start preschool program; however, we are adjusting the actual enrollment to 56 student seats which
lowers the student to adult ratio. This adjustment is being made through what is called a zero slot conversion,
supported by Head Start, which allows us to maintain full funding while ensuring reduced class sizes.

By making this adjustment, we are being proactive with enrollment trends and can maintain full funding, to
continue to provide our youngest students with early learning opportunities while also meeting the developmental
and individual needs of our students as, enrollment trends shift.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. SJUSD 2025-26 EHS Exhibit A-1
2. SJUSD 2025-26 HS Exhibit A-1
3. SJUSD - 2025-2026 Y2 Program Narrative_Application Final
4. SJUSD 2025-26-Exhibit-E-HS EHS List-of-Centers
5. SJUSD 2025-26 Early Head Start Budget Narrative
5. SJUSD 2025-26 Head Start Budget Narrative
7. SJUSD 2025-26 Head Start & Early Head Start Budget
8. ECE ORG Chart and Calendars 2025-2026
9. ECE Acronyms

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A

 ‭class) resulting in a 1:8 ratio.‬
  ‭2) LDO/WRAP classes are a collaboration between Head Start and State/CDE and operate under an ACF-approved‬
   ‭class-size to enroll up to 24 children per classroom.‬

     b) What centers/school sites and community zip codes will be affected by the change?
        Closures/Reduced Enrollment:
            •   Please identify the centers that will close or will have reduced enrollment.


                The following classrooms will close:
                1) General Davie Rm 14 (1727T)
                2) General Davie Rm 16 (1227X)
                3) Grand Oaks Rm 6 (1710R)
                4) Howe Rm J1(1725Y)


                The following classrooms will be reduced from 24 to 16:
                1) Howe Rm J2 (1725 S)
                2) Ralph Richardson Rm 3 (1719R)
                3) Sunrise Rm 2 (1746S)


            •   What zip codes will be affected?
                95864, 95825, 95608, 95610
            •   What is the justification for the change? Please cite data from updated community
                assessment, nearby TK schools, district enrollment trends, self-assessment results
                including enrollment trends, ongoing monitoring results, or from using data for
                continuous improvement as described in 1302.102(b)-(c).
                San Juan Unified School District (SJUSD) is closing the General Davie classrooms
                (95864) because the interest and waitlist data do not support the number of classrooms
                that SJUSD has available on campus. By closing classrooms and continuing to offer
                four classrooms, the agency more accurately meets the shifting needs of the community.
                In September 2024, after a summer of intentional recruitment efforts for the 95864 area
                code, the eligibility list had 33 students. At that time, 51 spots were still not filled.
                January 2025 enrollment data showed only 15 students on the eligibility list with the
                site at only 87% enrollment.

                                                                                                            42
           SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                         2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
        Grand Oaks (95621) is closing due to the TK on campus that was opened up. It was
        previously a low enrollment area, and then TK started, and enrollment continued to
        decline. The TK central enrollment waitlists were shared with the ECE Head Start
        department. These lists showed that Grand Oaks had a low waiting list (only eight
        students) for TK and confirmed that it is generally a low enrollment area for 3—and 4-
        year-olds.
        The Howe campus (95825) currently has four preschool classrooms, 3 of which are
        Head Start and one state-funded. The central district is in dire need of a classroom for a
        TK program. Howe J1 will be repurposed into a TK classroom to continue to serve 4-
        year-olds in SJUSD. Due to the addition of the TK at Howe, there is also a reduction in
        class size in Howe J2 from 24 to 16. With TK on campus, the number of 3-year-olds in
        the preschool program will increase. Reducing Howe J2 to 16 will ensure stronger
        safety and supervision for a class with a majority of 3-year-olds and will also avoid an
        enrollment cap on the classroom.
        Ralph Richardson (95608) Rm 3 and Sunrise (95610) Rm 2 are being reduced due to
        lower community interest, as shown by eligibility lists and enrollment data. In
        September 2024, the Sunrise campus for three classrooms only had 14 students on the
        eligibility lists, and the Ralph Richardson campus for three classrooms only had four
        people on the eligibility lists. Many families that are interested in Marvin Marshall are
        offered Ralph Richardson, which is where a majority of the enrollment comes from.
    •   Are there other early childhood programs available nearby for Head Start-eligible
        eligible families? Please identify the HS, preschool, and childcare available and the
        distance (in mileage) from the center that will close.
        The General Davie and Howe closures still provide Head Start classrooms. Howe will
        have three classrooms, and General Davie will have four. Mariposa Head Start Center
        will be in the Grand Oaks area, only 1.2 miles from the campus.

According to the Sacramento County Community Assessment data, there is a high need in all of
these areas based on the percentage of families receiving SNAP:
          95608 – 58.8%
          95610 – 49.7%
          95621 – 49.6%
          95628 – 46.6%
          95662 – 53.0%
          95825 – 60/9%
          95841 – 48.3%
          95842 – 69.5%

These zip codes serve children in the San Juan Unified Head Start program. They are also
identified as Priority 1 in the Sacramento County Local Child Care Planning Council for
preschool and infant/toddler care, indicating the highest need for child care.

According to the Sacramento County Community Assessment, in 2024, there were 567,230
households, 29% of which were households with children. The population estimate for children
and youth under age 25 is 494,986, of which 115,794 are children ages 0 through 5, comprising
7.3% of the total population. Based on the California Department of Finance baseline
projections, the following are the estimated number of children under the age of 5 in 2025:
18,168 are age zero (increased from 2024), 18,110 are age one (Decreased from 2024), 18,413
are age two (Decreased from 2024), 19,334 are age three (Increased from 2024), and 18,696 are
age four (Decreased from 2024).

Sacramento County’s population in 2024 is estimated at 1,578,938, making it the 8th largest
county in the state by population, according to the Community Assessment. With such a large
population, the county's diversity continues to grow. The chart below compares San Juan
Unified School District’s Early Head Start and Head Start student data for the 23-24 school year
to Sacramento County race demographics.

     Race                               Sacramento County SJUSD EHS SJUSD HS
     American Indian/Alaskan native           1%            0%        0.1%

     Asian                                    19%          18%         78%

     Biracial/Multiracial                     14%           4%         7%

     Black/African American                   10%          11%         12%

     Native Hawaiian/Pacific Islander         1%            0%        0.4%

     White                                    42%          51%         48%

     Other Race/Unspecified                   12%          13%         9%

            SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                 CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                          2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)

 San Juan Unified Head Start and Early Head Start programs have a large population of English
 Language Learners (ELL). During the 2023-2024 school year, 75% of the students were ELL
 students in the Early Head Start Program. In the Head Start program, 63% of the students
 qualified as ELL. Currently, the San Juan Unified TK-12 student population consists of 8,712
 English Language Learners, 22% of the student population. The chart below demonstrates how
 San Juan Unified Head Start and Early Head Start primary languages as compared to
 Sacramento County.


                 Language                      Sacramento County SJUSD EHS SJUSD HS
                 English                             68%            29%         39%
                 Spanish                             13%            19%         13%
                 Middle Eastern/Arabic         No available data    39%         39%
                 East Asian/Pacific Islander         9%             0%           7%
                 European/Slavic                     9%             12%          7%
                 Other                               1%             1%          0.4%


In the 2023-2024 school year, San Juan Unified Head Start served 17 (2%) students who were
either homeless or in foster care and seven (3%) students in Early Head Start. Currently, the San
Juan Unified TK-12 has served 1818 homeless students in the TK-12 classrooms, which is 5% of
the overall student population. 129 Foster children were served, which is .3%. Additionally,
seven students (3%) with Individual Family Service Plans (IFSP) were served in the San Juan
Unified Early Head Start program, and 104 students (13%) with Individualized Education Plans
(IEP) were served.

The San Juan Unified Head Start and Early Head Start support families with their health needs.
In the 2023-2024 school year, there were 523 (63%) Head Start families with medical homes
(homes where families participated in regularly scheduled well-child checks) at the time of
enrollment; by the end of enrollment, the percentage increased by 9%, with 597 families or 72%
of families with medical homes. In Early Head Start, there were 35 families with medical homes
at the time of enrollment, which increased to 96 by the end of enrollment, a 25% increase overall
due to the support of the staff working with the families. Additional health needs of San Juan
Unified students were identified in the 23-24 school year. Head Start student data showed 134
students had chronic conditions, and 30% had Asthma. 13% of students fell into the obese or
overweight category, and 7% of the students were classified as underweight. Of the 731 students
who received a professional oral examination, 103 (12%) needed oral treatment. Thanks to the
resources and staff support, 94% of those students could receive treatment.

San Juan Unified Head Start follows the traditional school year schedule, with 6.5 hours of care
for students ten months of the year. Head Start serves children ages 3 to 5. Early Head Start
programs provide 7 hours of care to children ages 0 to 3. Additionally, Early Head Start offers
both 10-month and 12-month care. The San Juan Unified Head Start program currently holds
507 students on the eligibility waitlist and 151 students on the eligibility waitlist for Early Head
Start, showing a great need in the San Juan Unified School District for Head Start services.
                                                                                                       46
                 SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                      CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                               2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)

     San Juan Unified is continuing to expand the TK options across the district. For the 25-26 school
     year, there will be 41 TK classrooms available to all families applying for the lottery. Eight of
     those TKs will offer a full-day program. 14 TKs will offer 4 hours and 19 will offer 3.3 hours.
     For the 24-25 school year, there are currently 35 TK classrooms available. The percentages of 4-
     year-olds in the Head Start program have decreased from the 60% of 4-year-olds in the 21-22
     school year when there were no TKs to the 24-25 school year that currently has 54%. San Juan
     Unified ECE predicts another decrease in 4-year-olds, with 41 TKs expected in the upcoming
     year, and the qualifying age will continue to drop.

3.    Proposed Program Option(s) and Funded Enrollment Slots (1302 Subpart B and the
      HSPPS Compliance Table)

                                     EARLY HEAD START

     San Juan Unified Early Head Start will operate a center-based option and a home-based option.
     The center-based option will have 12 toddler classrooms funded by EHS and CCTR.

                 OPTION 1 - EARLY HEAD START - CENTER-BASED MODELS

     Twelve Early Head Start classrooms will provide toddler care for 96 students ages 18 to 36 months
     utilizing CCTR and Early Head Start funds. Four classrooms will be 10-month programs, with the
     center open for ten months and home visits during the summer. The other eight classrooms will have
     the center open for 12 months to meet the community's needs. The program will measure students'
     progress toward early learning outcomes using the Desired Results Development Profile (DRDP)
     progress monitoring tool. This tool provides data on student learning and development in the fall,
     winter, and spring. Parents are offered parent conferences twice yearly to discuss their child’s
     progress. Additionally, parents are surveyed once a year to provide feedback on their child’s growth.

          OPTION 2 – HEAD START –LDO with CLASS-SIZE WAIVER (EHS TRANSFERS)

    The Head Start LDO option #2 will provide preschool for three and four-year-olds and have 48 slots.
    Head Start funds will fund this LDO. In addition, these classrooms will utilize a waiver to have up to
    20 three-year-old students in a classroom as long as the additional students (past 17 students) come
    from an EHS program with no other options. This supports the transition requirements outlined in the
    Head Start performance standards. To offer continuity of care, Ralph Richardson duration classrooms
    will accept transfers from Marvin Marshall EHS classrooms. Davie duration classrooms will accept
    transfers from Davie EHS classrooms. Many EHS students from Marvin Marshall transferred to
    Ralph Richardson after filling the slots. The Marvin Marshall site fills up quickly, and Ralph
    Richardson, 1.7 miles away, is the closest site for many of these families. The program will measure
    students' progress toward early learning outcomes using the DRDP progress monitoring tool. This
    tool provides data development for student learning and development in the fall and spring. Parents
    are offered parent conferences twice yearly to discuss their child’s progress. Additionally, parents are
    surveyed once a year to provide feedback on their child’s growth.

    Program (CSPP) and Head Start funds. The program will measure students' progress toward early
    learning outcomes using the DRDP progress monitoring tool. This tool provides data on student
    learning and development in the fall and spring. Parents are offered parent conferences twice yearly

Summary of Proposed Program Changes in Funding

Head Start Zero Slot Conversion
      Proposal: Zero slot conversion to retain the funds of 72 slots within the program and reduce Head
      Start slots in the classrooms by 56 (72 if not approved). Funding for the 16 slots was retained for the
      24-25 school year and utilized for extra staffing support in classrooms with high-need students. The
      reduction in slots includes classroom closures as well as class-size reduction. Class-size reduction in
      5 classes from 24 to 16 (8 slots in 5 classes = 40 slots) and closure of 2 Head Start classrooms (32
      slots)

Agreement with Grantee: San Juan Unified may retain the funding of the 72 slots displaced in the
class size reduction of five classes from 24 to 16 and the closure of two classrooms in low-enrollment
sites that have competing TKs to allow for stronger enrollment in nearby San Juan Unified Head Start
programs.

Funding impact: Retaining funding for 72 HS slots - $774,295

Funds to be retained for 2025-26 Program Year:
Total HS classroom slot reduction = 72*
Total retained = $774,295
*56 if Mid-Year Application not approved

Rationale for Retention of Funding Head Start

San Juan Unified Head Start continues to work in partnership with upper management on Transitional
Kindergarten planning. The final year for implementation is the 25-26 school year; 41 TKs across the
district have been confirmed, with the possibility of 3 more still in the planning process. The
continued growth of the TK program has impacted enrollment numbers and the ages of the children
who are requesting Head Start preschool services. Enrollment of four-year-old students in the
program has decreased by 9% over the last two years. Long-term planning for sustainability and high
quality of the program requires a program design that projects a majority of three-year-old students in
the classroom. A smaller class size dramatically contributes to the success of a classroom that is
mostly 3 years old. Additional staff is needed as some three-year-old students require one-on-one
diaper changes and toilet training. Retention of funding is necessary because even though the class
size decreased, the costs to run the classroom remain the same, if not increase, due to extra support
needed.

Additionally, classroom closures in areas with competing TKs that have reduced enrollment ensure
that the program achieves full enrollment starting in August. In February 2025, enrollment was 95%
(97% if the mid-year program change is approved), with 675 students enrolled. While enrollment is
strong, across the 35 classrooms for the Head Start program, there are only 50 students on the waiting
lists. By reducing enrollment slots by 56 (72 if a mid-year application is not approved), we are
ensuring that our program will be fully enrolled in August and that we will have healthy waitlists
across the district throughout the year.

This “right sizing” of the Head Start preschool will ensure that all new Head Start performance
standards and Office of Head Start initiatives can be met. This is another important reason for the
retention of funds. Support staffing has been analyzed according to program needs, and all positions
that will not be needed next year have been submitted to the Human Resources department. In
examining the new performance standards, support staff responsible for providing families with
resources and mental health support could not be removed from the program. Funds are needed to
make sure we have the support staff required. Additionally, the union negotiated a teacher salary
increase finalized in August, and retention of funds is greatly needed to continue supporting teacher
salaries. Without the retention of funds, the overall sustainability of the program is at risk.

San Juan Unified has had a highly rated Head Start preschool program for many years. In the recent
parent satisfaction survey sent out in January 2025, data showed that when asked how satisfied the

                                                                                                          53
                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
   families were with the Head Start program, 73% were Very Satisfied, and the remaining 27% were
   Satisfied. The parent survey was provided in 7 languages to ensure all families had a voice.

   The Head Start Preschool program teachers are all required to have their Bachelor’s degree, and
   many have continuing education units. The staff has monthly and optional training to support student
   behavior, IEP support, and regular program updates. Additional one-on-one training is always
   available to any teachers or CDAs seeking support. All facilities are licensed and meet the regulations
   for square footage and the safety of the students. Yearly safety inspections are conducted and
   followed up with needed maintenance and upgrades. Quarterly safety and supervision unannounced
   visits are conducted as well.

6. Eligibility, Recruitment, Selection, Enrollment, and Attendance (1302.13, 1302.14, 1302.15,
and 1302.16):

Please address both center-based and home-based programs.

•   What is going well in your program for this year, 2024-2025? Please describe by citing 3 data
    points or another source of information (for example, ADA, monthly enrollment, waiting list).

    1) The January Enrollment of Head Start was 95%, and Early Head Start was 93%. This is a
       15% increase from January 2024 – Head Start was 80%, and Early Head Start was 86%
    2) The ECE recruitment team participated in three back-to-school nights at the beginning of the
       year and continues to participate in the new district Family and Community Engagement
       (FACE) initiative, the Community Care Hub, which travels around the school district.
    3) San Juan is working closer with the communication department, which has resulted in two
       special interest stories featuring ECE staff, one marketing video, and two event highlights on
       all district social media platforms.

•   What did not go well or as planned? What are the challenges you faced this year? Please describe.
    What changes or adaptations did you make to address these challenges?

    1) The enrollment team lost two technicians during the fall enrollment peak. One position was
       filled in November 2024, and the second one will be filled by March 2025, in time for the
       beginning of the 25-26 school year enrollment process.
    2) Early Head Start enrollment was much higher than last year (86% in January 2024 vs. 93% in
       January 2025), but the numbers had to be capped due to staffing challenges. Once the human
       resources department has sorted out the staffing challenges, enrollment will be close to 100%.

•   Describe specific efforts to actively locate, recruit, and enroll vulnerable children, including
    children with disabilities, children experiencing homelessness, families in SNAP, and children in
    foster care.

    Due to the vast resources available across the San Juan Unified School District, intra-district
    department partnerships have helped the ECE department recruit and enroll families in need.
    Ongoing meetings around intentional communication strategies between the Special Education
    Department and the McKinney-Vento Department have supported enrolling more families. The
    Special Education Department refers families with disabilities to the ECE department when the
    blended part-day special education preschool program does not fit the families’ needs. When
    children enroll in EHS/HS services, the inclusion content specialist oversees the care management
    and IFSP and IEP support for the families.

    The FACE department has created the "Community Care Hub" monthly event, where a mobile
    resource fair allows families to access essential tools for student success. Food, diapers, learning
    tools, and community resources are provided. Support for enrollment, Parent Portal, school

                                                                                                           55
            SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                 CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                          2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
    communication, and navigating district programs and services are also included. SCWs and the
    Family Engagement content specialist participate with a table every month to recruit families to
    the Early Head Start and Head Start programs. ECE Head Start has worked closely with the
    District Foster Youth Liaison and supplied them with enrollment flyers for all of their clients.

    School Community Workers' work, in partnership with the Attendance Improvement Program,
    has invited the ECE department to attend School Attendance Review Board meetings. At these
    meetings, ECE can provide information to families regarding infant, toddler, and preschool
    programs that may support the attendance of their siblings in the TK-12 school system.

    NEW! Updated Performance Standard Requirements
•   1302.12 (i) (1): How are you implementing the housing adjustment (excessive housing costs)?

    The ERSEA officer has trained admissions and Family Service Technicians (AFSTs) from SETA
    on tools and resources shared by the Office of Head Start and ChildPlus. If the family is not
    income or categorically eligible, AFSTs have been trained to calculate the housing adjustment to
    help some higher-income families become eligible for the program.

•   1302.13, 1302 15 (g) What changes have you made/will you make to incorporate modern
    technologies to assist in the enrollment process, streamline, and reduce administrative and
    paperwork burden to families?

    San Juan Unified ERSEA team is working on revamping a new online eligibility form so families
    do not have to come in person to start the process of being waitlisted or enrolled. Updating and
    reducing questions to capture essential questions will happen by the end of the 24-25 school year.
    The Online eligibility form is shared via QR code on physical and digital flyers for easy access
    for all families.

•   1302.14 (a)(6) How are you incorporating/will incorporate the enrollment of eligible children of
    staff members as part of the selection criteria?

    SETA, the Grantee, has updated the selection criteria for both EHS and HS with changes to
    incorporate staff members within the selection criteria.

•   1302.16 (a)(2)(v) Describe how the program examines/will examine barriers to regular
    attendance, such as access to safe and reliable transportation, and where possible, provide or
    facilitate transportation for the child if needed.

    As part of an LEA, the San Juan Unified School District ECE department does not provide
    transportation. Using ChildPlus attendance, an absence code is explicitly designated for families
    who do not attend class due to transportation issues. School Community Workers also work with
    families to find transportation support at the San Juan Unified FACE department or the
    Department of Human Assistance serving Sacramento County.



                                                                                                         56
            SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                 CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                          2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
•   1302.17 9 (a) Describe the program’s policy on suspension and expulsion and how it ensures that
    suspension is a measure of last resort and how the programs explore and document all steps
    taken to address concerns and support the child’s re-entry and continued participation in the
    program.

    In San Juan Unified ECE, numerous steps are taken to support the individualized needs of the
    children and families in the Early Head Start and Head Start Program. Below is the process that
    San Juan Unified follows when there are behavior challenges in the classroom:

    Teacher Consultation/Referral Process:
    San Juan Unified ECE teachers use the Implementation of Successful Classroom Management
    and Mental Health Referral Process guide. Mental health and consultation services are offered
    through a referral process from the teacher and family. A classroom observation form is filled out
    to invite the Mental Health Therapist (MHT) into the classroom. The MHT will work with the
    family and teacher on concerns about the child and set a plan for either behavior or to connect the
    family with other resources or referrals, if needed.

    Step 1:
    Teachers will implement Program Guidelines on best practices for successful classroom
    management for children presenting with behavior concerns:

    a. Redirection
    b. Offering choices
    c. Modeling acceptable behavior
    d. Natural consequences (when safe and appropriate)
    e. Logical consequences that result in positive learning experiences.

    Step 2:
    If a child’s behavior persists after step 1 has been implemented, it is crucial to complete
    the Student Behavior Log thoroughly (consistently for one week) to capture patterns of behavior
    and interventions accurately. Additional review of the implemented Second Step intervention
    cards is recommended.

    Step 3:
    The teacher and the child’s parent/guardian will hold a conference to address the child’s
    behaviors and collaboratively agree on implementing a Classroom Strategy Plan (CSP) with a
    minimum 2-week trial. The team will now complete a Parent/Teacher Conference form. The team
    may consult with Mental Health Therapist Jason Nigl, LMFT, regarding creating and
    implementing the CSP. The teacher must obtain a parent-signed Child Observation Permission
    Form to enable MHT to observe the child.

    Step 4:
    After the two-week trial period of implementing the Classroom Strategy Plan, if it is determined
    that the plan isn’t effectively changing the behavior(s), the team should consult with the MHT.
    The MHT will review the child’s ASQ-SE, Parent/Teacher Conference form, Student Behavior
    Log, and the Classroom Strategy Plan. The MHT will then do follow-up observations, provide

                                                                                                          57
                 SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                      CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                               2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
        additional classroom strategies/interventions, follow up with implementation and ongoing
        monitoring, and/or facilitate a referral for counseling services.

        With all of these steps and strategies utilized, San Juan Unified has been able to support the needs
        of the students enrolled without the need to terminate or suspend enrollment. Parent partnership is
        a key aspect of all the steps, with continuous and open communication with the parents. If the
        need ever occurs where a child is not benefitting from the program, decisions to change programs
        will be made in partnership with parents and will be viewed as the very last resort.


7. Education and Child Development (1302 Subpart C)

Please address both center-based and home-based programs.

•   What is going well in your program for this year 2024-2025? Please describe by citing 3 data points
    or another source of information (for example, percentage of completed developmental screenings
    within 45 days, DRDP, CLASS).

    •   36% of preschool children are rated as Building Middle for ATL-REG 6: Engagement and Persistence, and
        39% are rated as Building Middle for SED 5: Symbolic and Sociodramatic Play, possibly reflecting an
        increased focus on SEL.
    •   Emotional Support domain scores for a sample of 13 classrooms observed averaged 6.54, Classroom
        Organization scores averaged 6.40, and Instructional Support scores averaged 3.38.
    •   All preschool CLASS assessments are completed for the year using the CLASS 2.0 PreK to grade 3 tool
        that observers were newly trained on this year.
    •   Currently, 50% of Infant/Toddler classes have completed ITERS class observations, with 100% to be
        completed by March 2025.
    •   100% of Infant/Toddler IDPs are completed online using Learning Genie to allow parents to read the IDPs
        in their preferred language.

•   What did not go well or as planned? What are the challenges you faced this year? Please describe.
    What changes or adaptations did you make to address these challenges?

    The planned adoption of the Learning Genie Action Planning feature for preschool classrooms had
    some unexpected technical issues due to transfers during or after the Fall rating period. Most teachers
    successfully completed the Action Plan and shared it with families before and during their
    conferences. Still, some had to complete it using the older Individualized Development Plan (IDP)
    form due to technical difficulties with this new approach. On a case-by-case basis, teachers
    collaborated with each other and/or received support from content specialists to complete the plans
    timely. An additional challenge was the lack of full classroom staffing, resulting in some DRDP
    assessments not being completed in a timely manner or thoroughly. Further training on DRDP
    assessment and Learning Genie best practices was offered to new preschool teachers and additional
    one-on-one support from content specialists and TOSAs.


                                                                                                                  58
                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
•   Describe any changes to the curriculum used, curricular enhancements, and/or significant adaptations
    (include home-based, if applicable).

    No changes were made to the curricula used, which are Creative Curriculum 6 and Second Step.
    Refresher training was offered for both, along with one-on-one support as needed. Teacher feedback
    was requested to help update the lesson plan form and guidance to better support implementation, and
    the resulting version was generally approved and is being phased into use.

•   Describe how you support teaching staff in implementing the curriculum with fidelity. How did you
    use ASQ, ASQ: SE screening results, DRDP, and classroom observations to support teaching staff in
    meeting curriculum fidelity?

    Teachers submit various paperwork during the year, including best practices checklists, lesson plan
    samples, and IDP tracking sheets, which are all reviewed to check for fidelity. In addition, DRDP
    assessment results are examined to check for trends that may indicate a need for additional training or
    support. This year, new teachers were given further support through one-on-one classroom
    observations and meetings from the content specialist to check for overall support needs, including
    curriculum and assessment support.

•   Describe group socializations to be offered. What changes have you made in the current year to
    increase the participation of families in socialization events (home-based only)?

    Group socializations for the Home-Based program include a parent meeting where many community
    resources are shared with parents, a snack, and social time with children and other families. The
    teachers create interactive centers and play areas that connect with what they are working on with the
    families. Descriptions of each activity are provided in the Socialization binder for families to know
    what each activity is about, and instructions, if needed, are posted. Families enjoy the activities with
    their children and engage in conversation with other families. One thing that occurred this year was
    that families were given a survey at the beginning of the year all about the socializations. Families
    were asked about their preferred meeting time and what activities they wanted to experience at the
    socializations. Parent feedback is also collected during the home visit after socialization. Two
    consistent meeting spots on either side of the district have been established this year to give families a
    familiar place to meet each time. School Community Workers are more involved in organizing guest
    speakers for parent meetings this year. All of these strategies have increased parent participation this
    year.

                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
    NEW! Updated Performance Standard Requirements
•   1302.41, 1302.42 (b), 1302.46 (b) Describe how the program consistently integrates mental health
    into all aspects of program service delivery

    San Juan Unified ECE values wellness and embeds mental health support into all aspects of the
    programs. See below for more details.

•   1302.45 (a), (b) Describe how the program uses a multidisciplinary approach to mental health and
    wellness support in the classroom- children, families, staff? Describe how mental health consultation
    services will be provided or made available at least once a month to children, center-based and home-
    based teaching staff.

    Mental health support for children and families starts during the Intake and Screening processes in
    the following ways:

    •   ASQ/ASQ SE—At the enrollment screening, the parent or caregiver completes a questionnaire to
        assess their child’s social-emotional wellness.
    •   Family Partnership Agreement—A Staff member meets with the family to review their current
        needs, strengths, and areas they would like to learn more about.
    •   Red Flag Screening Checklist- A checklist generated to capture details of an elevated ASQ-SE
        questionnaire. If concerns from the ASQ-SE arise, the checklist form is completed and forwarded
        to MHT to assess and determine the specific mental health interventions necessary.

    Social Emotional Competencies Curriculum Routines and Resources support the classroom
    environments with explicit curriculum that teaches children the appropriate self-regulation skills and
    tools needed to lower the risk of mental health issues in the future. These curricula, routines, and
    resources are supported in the following ways:

    A committee of the Preschool Administration, Mental Health Therapist, Inclusion, and Education
    Content teams meets monthly to align on training and curricular initiatives supporting Social-
    Emotional Competencies (SECs). Preschool staff have received training on the following:

    •   A Second Step Refresher
    •   Supporting Students with Challenging Behavior
    •   The Behavior Referral Process
    •   Strategies for supporting students with Autism Spectrum Disorder (ASD)

    To further ensure a shared understanding of SECs, the preschool lesson plan template has been
    updated to explicitly include Second Step lessons and objectives that outline how SECs can be
    integrated throughout the day. These ongoing efforts aim to strengthen social-emotional learning in
    our classrooms and provide the best possible support for our students.

    In the Early Head Start Programs, one cohort of 8 teachers was trained on the Teaching Pyramid
    Systemic Framework that promotes social and emotional development in the classroom through
    routine and relationship building. The Teaching Pyramid provides teachers with the tools to set up a


                                                                                                             60
                   SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                        CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                                 2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
       safe and nurturing environment where young infants and toddlers can develop the social emotional
       skills they need to be successful in their interactions with others and develop self-confidence.


       San Juan Unified also provides explicit parent education that supports strong mental health in
       children and families. MHT provides parent workshops on a variety of rotating topics, including but
       not limited to Limit Setting and reinforcing Positive Behaviors, Self-Esteem Building, Emotional
       Wellness, Mindful Parenting, The Power of Presence in Parenting, Sleep and Behavior, Attention on
       Intention, and Bonding and Attachment.

       The MHT and the School Community Workers distribute Mental Health referrals and resources. All
       services and resources are documented and tracked within Child Plus and internal tracking sheets.
       MHT also holds bi-weekly collaboration meetings with the Inclusion Content Specialist to address
       continuity of care and overall program support needs. The MHT works full-time for San Juan Unified
       and is available daily to all families for any emergency or non-emergency mental health consultation.

8. Health (1302 Subpart D)

   Please address both center-based and home-based programs.

   •   What is going well in your program for this year 2024-2025? Please describe by citing 3 data points
       or another source of information (for example, the percentage of children with up-to-date health
       screenings, dental exams, follow-up treatment, etc.).

       •   Data from the Child Plus report 3015 for Head Start students in November showed 614 students
           missing health requirements, and in December, it improved to only 326 students missing health
           requirements.
       •   As of December 2024, 439 students have received oral health screenings through our partnership
           with Early Smiles.
       •   Comprehensive health screenings are held weekly, which include height, weight, vision, hearing,
           blood pressure, and hemoglobin checks, along with consultations from Credentialed School
           Nurses and follow-up on missing health requirements. As of December 2024, direct services for
           814 students and their families have been provided for the 2024-2025 school year.

   •   What did not go well or as planned? What are the challenges you faced this year? Please describe.
       What changes or adaptations did you make to address these challenges?

           •   Data from ChildPlus report 9711 for Early Head Start students in November showed 68
               students missing health requirements, and in December, it increased to 86 students missing
               health requirements.
                   ▪ To address this challenge, the Early Head Start Health Assistant has been attending
                       socialization days, parent meetings, and one-on-one communication to request missing
                       health requirements.
           •   Several students have been unable to obtain immunizations at required intervals due to an
               apparent vaccine shortage within the community.
                   ▪ To address this challenge, the health team has provided community immunization
                       resources to obtain missing immunizations.

                                                                                                               61
                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
•   Describe how your program will, in partnership with parents, meet the oral health, nutritional, mental
    health, social and emotional well-being, and health status and care needs of children that are
    developmentally, culturally, and linguistically appropriate and support each child’s growth and
    school readiness.

    All students' health/nutritional histories, physical exams/healthy child well-child checks, dental
    exams, and immunization records are collected at registration and reviewed by the health team before
    enrollment. If health concerns are noted at review, the student’s health file is forwarded to the
    Credentialed School Nurse for follow-up as needed. Health forms are provided in multiple languages,
    and interpreting services are utilized as needed. Health screening events are held throughout the
    summer and weekly during the school year, with accommodations made based on family needs. The
    screening process includes, but is not limited to, obtaining height, weight, vision, hearing, blood
    pressure, and hemoglobin. The Credentialed School Nurse is available for consultation, education,
    and anticipatory guidance if needed. We partner with Early Smiles/Center for Oral Health during the
    school year to provide screenings to all students onsite for all programs.

•   Describe how your program will ensure up-to-date child health status, ongoing care, and timely
    follow-up care. How do you examine collected health data to support families needing additional
    support to meet health requirements and access medical or dental treatment when needed?

    In conjunction with parents and community partnerships, San Juan Unified ensures all children are up
    to date for preventative care according to the current pediatric periodicity table in health and dental
    areas (Bright Futures). If there is any area where a child is not up to date, the parent is given
    education, resources, or other assistance in the preferred language, if available, or through the
    interpreter line. The child's status is tracked in the Child Plus software system, as well as by health
    assistants and credentialed school nurses. Reminder calls, letters, emails, and other resources are sent
    to the caregivers if a child is not up to date. The health team follows up with students who have
    atypical screening results. A Health Care Plan is created and implemented for any student with a
    particular health need; the nurse trains classroom staff on the student's needs. The health team
    collaborates with SETA and the Health Services Advisory Committee to find solutions for any
    challenges in receiving preventative screenings within the community. The San Juan Unified
    immunization clinic and other community resources are utilized as needed.
