Mental health support for children and families starts during the Intake and Screening processes in
the following ways:

•   During the Health Screening portion of the screening process, families are allowed to speak with
    a Registered nurse and ask any questions regarding physical and mental health. Nurses will refer
    to the MHT and Disabilities Content should any concerns arise in conversation or general
    observations with the family.
•   ASQ/ASQ SE—At the enrollment screening, the parent or caregiver completes a questionnaire to
    assess their child’s social-emotional wellness.
•   Family Partnership Agreement—A Staff member meets with the family to review their current
    needs, strengths, and areas they would like to learn more about.
•   Red Flag Screening Checklist- A checklist generated to capture details of an elevated ASQ-SE
    questionnaire. If concerns from the ASQ-SE arise, the checklist form is completed and forwarded
    to MHT to assess and determine the specific mental health interventions necessary.

Social Emotional Competencies Curriculum Routines and Resources support the classroom
environments with explicit curriculum that teaches children the appropriate self-regulation skills and
tools needed to lower the risk of mental health issues in the future. These curricula, routines, and
resources are supported in the following ways:

A committee of the Preschool Administration, Mental Health Therapist, Inclusion, and Education
Content teams meets monthly to align on training and curricular initiatives supporting Social-
Emotional Competencies (SECs). Preschool staff have received training on the following:

•   A Second Step Refresher
•   Supporting Students with Challenging Behavior
•   The Behavior Referral Process
•   Strategies for supporting students with Autism Spectrum Disorder (ASD)

To further ensure a shared understanding of SECs, the preschool lesson plan template has been
updated to explicitly include Second Step lessons and objectives that outline how SECs can be
integrated throughout the day. These ongoing efforts aim to strengthen social-emotional learning in
our classrooms and provide the best possible support for our students.

In the Early Head Start Programs, one cohort of 8 teachers was trained on the Teaching Pyramid
Systemic Framework that promotes social and emotional development in the classroom through
routine and relationship building. The Teaching Pyramid provides teachers with the tools to set up a
safe and nurturing environment where young infants and toddlers can develop the social emotional
skills they need to successfully interact with others and develop self-confidence.

San Juan Unified also provides explicit parent education that supports strong mental health in
children and families. MHT provides parent workshops on a variety of rotating topics, including but
not limited to Limit Setting and reinforcing Positive Behaviors, Self-Esteem Building, Emotional
Wellness, Mindful Parenting, The Power of Presence in Parenting, Sleep and Behavior, Attention on
Intention, and Bonding and Attachment.

The MHT and the School Community Workers distribute Mental Health referrals and resources. All
services and resources are documented and tracked within Child Plus and internal tracking sheets.
                                                                                                         63
                   SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                        CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                                 2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
       The MHT also holds bi-weekly collaboration meetings with the Inclusion Content Specialist to
       address continuity of care and overall program support needs. The MHT works full-time for San Juan
       Unified and is available daily to all families for emergency or non-emergency mental health
       consultations.

9. Family and Community Engagement (1302 Subpart E)

   Please address both center-based and home-based programs.
   •
       What is going well in your program for this year 2024-2025? Please cite 3 data points or another
       source of information to illustrate why it is going well (for example, number of completed FPAs,
       number of community partnerships, percentage of families using Ready Rosie).

          •   San Juan Unified ECE Parent workshops on various topics have been offered in the district's
              different regions. Fifty-eight families have attended the six workshops.
          •   As of January 2025, 49% of classrooms have a Policy Committee representative. This is only
              1% of the Year 1 goal of 50% of classrooms being representatives. Recruitment efforts are
              continuing by support staff, teachers, and current representatives. One factor that contributed
              to higher percentages of representatives this year was the summer offering of the program
              orientation that highlighted the benefits of being on the Policy Committee.
          •   This year, 18 Parent Cafes were offered in English and Spanish, and 50 parents have attended
              since the program started in October.

   •   What did not go well or as planned? What are the challenges you faced this year? What changes or
       adaptations did you make to address these challenges?

       The beginning of the year was inundated with more mandates, which has caused delays in some of
       the initiatives planned for this year. Additionally, the staff turnover of a key secretary position that
       supported the policy committee greatly impacted the time needed to cover job duties and train new
       staff. With more focus on Policy Committee initiatives, Ready Rosie initiatives from the previous
       year were not the priority. The Family Engagement Content could send out playlists and update the
       Ready Rosie database, but not as regularly as needed. Moving forward, the Family Engagement
       Content will ensure that the Ready Rosie database is current and that playlists are updated monthly.
       Additionally, volunteer tracking needed to be updated, and a new digital tracking system was created
       and implemented in January of 2025. The list of volunteers on the tracking sheet will be utilized for
       recruitment for the volunteer committee.

   •   Describe key program strategies for building trusting and respectful relationships with families and
       providing program environments and services that are welcoming and culturally and linguistically
       responsive to families, including those specific to fathers.

       All families are welcomed into the program with kindness, respect, and excitement. Even before
       families enter the program, any family that visits the office to inquire about enrollment is met with
       excitement from the staff for the opportunity to serve them. Building trusting relationships starts with
       the enrollment interview and when families come for summer screening. School Community Workers
       meet families at summer screening and continue building the relationships when they meet with
       families to create their goal for the year. Families are more open to contacting their SCW for support

                                                                                                                  64
                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
    when the relationship is built. To make families feel comfortable, if they prefer to communicate in
    their home language, translation services are requested from San Juan Central if needed or provided
    by School Community Resource Assistants (SCRAs) or Bilingual Instructional Assistants (BIAs).
    Bilingual Instructional Assistants (BIAs) are available in the classrooms to help children feel
    welcomed in their language and help teachers communicate with parents. San Juan Unified ECE hires
    SCWs, BIAs, and SCRAs to support our families with language support as needed. Additional
    translation tools, such as the Language Line, are also utilized by that staff to help families get the
    necessary information. All forms are translated into multiple languages based on the language needs
    of the families, such as Dari/Farsi, Pashto, Russian, Ukrainian, and Spanish.

    Important community events are shared with all families to help them feel more included. San Juan
    Unified ECE organizes some events, such as the Fall Literacy Festival, which over 400 families
    attended, and the Male Involvement event in the Spring, which 30 families attended. Other
    community event information is collected by the School Community Workers and shared with
    families via email, flyer, or during the monthly parent meeting.

•   Describe engagement activities to support parent-child relationships, child development, family
    literacy, and language development, including supporting bilingualism and bi-literacy.

    San Juan Unified holds an annual Fall Literacy festival each October, inviting current and potential
    families across the district to participate. Over 400 families attended in 2024. Many resources are
    available for families, such as food boxes, healthy snacks, free books, and 2nd hand clothing in
    various sizes. Families can participate in community age-appropriate activities such as games, a
    dance party, temporary body art, arts and crafts, picking pumpkins at the pumpkin patch, and
    taking family pictures in the pumpkin patch. A librarian hosted story time on the grass, and the San
    Juan Unified School District Family and Community Engagement (FACE) department also had its
    resource mobile, which has resources to support families, such as upcoming FACE events and
    giveaways.

    Regarding specific programs, the EHS Home-based socializations have been scheduled
    strategically at some of the libraries within the San Juan Unified boundaries to demonstrate to
    families what resources and activities their local libraries have for them and their children.
    Additionally, home visitors bring books weekly to share with their families. In the EHS centers,
    parents are encouraged to take books home and read to their children. Books are also read in the
    classroom to children throughout the day. In the HS programs, story time is integrated into the
    daily schedule, and a library center is utilized daily, where children can explore books with each
    other, on their own, or with an adult.

    Our BIAs support bilingualism and biliteracy. They can speak with students and families in their
    native languages and read with students in the classrooms.

•   How are you utilizing Ready Rosie to engage families?

    Families are introduced and signed up for Ready Rosie at their classroom orientation. This year,
    support staff provided program orientations for many families at a central location during the
    summer. During the summer program orientation, staff demonstrated how Ready Rosie works so
    families can see all the program's benefits. Reviewing how to accept the invite, changing the


                                                                                                             65
                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
    language preference, and turning on notifications via text or email were essential features to review to
    increase parent engagement with the app.

    The Family Engagement Content Specialist creates the classrooms and gets the monthly Child Plus
    report to upload new families to their classrooms. The Content Specialist checks the pending invites
    monthly and ensures they are resent if they are pending. Families receive weekly automated videos
    and additional videos sent by the Content Specialist monthly.

•   What are your program strategies for family partnership services, including conducting the family
    assessment and family partnership process and aligning activities to the Parent, Family, and
    Community Engagement Framework outcomes?

    To ensure all family needs are met, the FPA process occurs during the screening process before the
    family starts the program. Families come through the office and can complete the FPA process
    individually with an SCW. During this process, the family can identify any emergency needs they
    may have and additional resources they would like to receive in the future. This process is part of
    enrollment and ensures no family is missed when beginning the program. After the initial FPA
    process, the SCWs will follow up with any needs and help the families create goals for the year. To
    reach all families, the SCWs use a variety of communication strategies, such as texting, emailing,
    phone calls, and in-person meetings. The SCW builds a trusting relationship and ensures that
    families’ needs are met by individualizing the communication method according to each family's
    preference. The SCWs work directly with the teachers and Family Engagement Content Specialist to
    ensure appropriate resources are provided to parents at the monthly parent meeting. The SCW also
    attends this meeting to continue connections with families and sometimes present information on
    various resources. The Content Specialist creates a schedule to ensure all the PFCE outcomes are
    covered throughout the year. San Juan Unified always works to communicate with families in their
    preferred language by using SCWs, teaching staff, BIAs, SCRAs, and Language Line. Families
    receive resources about events that are happening in the community, as well as health and wellness
    resources. SCWs work with families throughout the year to align their goals with the PFCE outcomes
    and provide resources to ensure they are set up and empowered to achieve their goals.

•   How do you track progress toward individual family goals and needs?

    Family Goals are tracked electronically through a Google form and Child Plus. The Google form is
    uploaded to Child Plus as an event, and updates on the event are provided throughout the year. SCWs
    continually follow up with families and their goals, allowing them to continue to self-reflect to see if
    they need additional support or shift their goals to meet their needs better. In the EHS home-based
    program, families discuss goals during their weekly visits, and the family goals are integrated into the
    visit plans that the visitor and parent build collaboratively.

•   Provide a few examples of community partnerships that facilitate access to services or resources in
    the community that are responsive to family partnership goals and children’s needs. Identify any
    challenges to necessary partnerships and how the program plans to address those challenges.

    San Juan Unified ECE works with the San Juan Unified Intervention/ Prevention Attendance
    Improvement and the Families and Community Engagement (FACE) departments. SCWs assist at
    attendance support meetings for San Juan families, and two content specialists have attended and

Some Challenges that San Juan Unified ECE has encountered are the following:
      Within the large San Juan Unified School District, Elementary and High Schools (TK-12) have more
      resources readily available since TK-12 is the primary focus.
      Due to the organization of the ECE department, using some San Juan Unified resources is difficult.
      Some resources, such as Talking Points, originally designed for use at a site, become more complex
      when over 20 sites need to be integrated. This fantastic communication tool currently can’t be set up
      for ECE.
      - Additionally, funding for these organizations is not always predictable. Last year, ECE lost a strong
      partnership with Deseret Industries, which had to close due to ongoing financial and staffing issues.

NEW! Updated Performance Standard Requirements
  • 1302.34 (b)(9) Describe how the program incorporates/will incorporate accessible communication
     methods and modalities when engaging with prospective and enrolled families (modernizing
     communication)

       San Juan ECE currently utilizes a digital Eligibility Form found online on the ECE enrollment
       website, which is connected to the QR code on all recruitment flyers and available on iPads in the
       registration office to fill out in person. This form starts the enrollment process and allows anyone to
       fill it out without coming to the office. Many families served do not have access to transportation, so
       it provides the accessibility they need. Additionally, translation support is always available in various
       ways – all essential forms are translated in Arabic, Farsi, Dari, and Spanish. Some are also available
       in Pashto, Ukrainian, and Russian. Translation can be done in person with a translator from ECE or
       translation services. The Language Line is also utilized.

       Once enrolled, families have a variety of communication methods with the teacher. Learning Genie
       allows Early Head Start parents to know all the essential daily routines such as eating, sleeping, and
       toileting. Learning Genie provides pictures and examples of learning for each child and offers two-
       way chat communication with a translation option for parents. In Head Start classrooms, Learning
       Genie is utilized to share pictures and examples of learning from the classroom. Both Early Head
       Start and Head Start utilize Learning Genie to observe and report to parents on the DRDP measures
       that the students are mastering or need more support with.

       Teachers communicate with parents in various ways tailored to parent preferences. Phone calls,
       emails, two-way messaging through Learning Genie, Video Conferencing Platforms, written
       communication, and in-person meetings allow teachers to meet parents where they are at.

   •   1302.41, 1302.42 (b), 1302.46 (b) Describe how the program consistently integrates mental health
       into all aspects of program service delivery.

       Mental health remains a high priority for San Juan Unified ECE and is integrated into all parent
       engagement matters. The MHT is always available to families needing emergency or general
       consultation. The families meet with multiple staff members when they start the enrollment process,
       and they are always looking for families in distress. If there are any signs of need from the family
       when they meet with the AFST to complete enrollment paperwork, the nurse, School Community
       Worker, or support staff during screening all staff are prepared to provide resources. Teachers are
       aware of resources and can contact the School Community Worker or MHT if they need the family.

       Social-emotional learning is also highly valued and shared with parents regularly, whether through
       parent–teacher conferences, parent meetings, policy committee meetings, or parent workshops. San
       Juan Unified ECE values the importance of early intervention and parent education.

                   SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START

                                 2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)

10. Services for Children with Disabilities (1302 Subpart F)

Please address both center-based and home-based programs.

   •   What is going well in your program for this year 2024-2025? Please cite 2 data points or another
       source of information (for example, percentage of children referred for IDEA services, number of
       children with IEP/IFSP).

          •   As of December 2024, inclusion placements for the 24-25 school year are 90% full. One
              additional spot was provided in a high-need area.
          •   An average of 65% of classrooms consistently submit referral tracking forms. An average of
              82% of classrooms submit Delivery of Service logs for students with IEPS.
          •   143 students were referred this year for initial screening with site SLP and/or identified for
              developmental monitoring via screening and assessment procedures.

   •   What did not go well or as planned? What are the challenges you faced this year? Please describe.
       What changes or adaptations did you make to address these challenges?

          •   The procedure for delivering ASQ results to the teacher in the classroom was disrupted due to
              staff turnover. ASQ screeners require several staff members to process and prepare the
              documents/data for staff and program use. Continuous training of new and current staff so that
              more than one person could take over if needed helped to remedy this issue.
          •   Initial timelines for presenting SECs to staff and parents proved challenging due to the various
              initiatives that were happening with safety and enrollment. Preparing and presenting SEC
              information to staff for parent conferences was adjusted to mirror an updated family training
              timeline. SEC information was presented in flyer form to PC members and staff with a pre-
              implementation survey to ensure consistency across the program. Additional parent training
              will be offered in the Spring.
          •   Finding placements for students with additional needs was challenging, as full program
              enrollment yielded fewer options. Families were provided options for services as close to
              parent preference as possible. Collaboration between ECE and the SPED department also
              provided additional goals and support for children with challenging behavior to help make
              transition and placement as successful as possible.

   •   Describe how your program will ensure full participation in program services and activities for
       enrolled children with disabilities, including but not limited to those eligible for services under IDEA
       and those who already have an IFSP or IEP.

          Early Head Start-

          San Juan Unified EHS programs provide ongoing documentation of each child’s development
          in the home and center-based programs. Using the Ages and Stages Questionnaire (ASQ 3 and
          ASQ 2 SE) series, center-based and home-based teachers will routinely screen child progress
          with families and collect observational data, family reporting, and relevant medical appointment
          feedback. Each child’s growth will also be assessed by support staff, using the same tools as
          needed to identify best practices for each student. Any child displaying developmental markers

                                                                                                                  69
         SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
              CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                       2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
below the assessment tool's threshold will be monitored more frequently, and families will be
provided with all results. Families will determine how any concerns will be addressed,
including but not limited to continuing to monitor development while providing individualized
lesson planning to support areas of concern, meeting with support staff (Teacher On Special
Assignment (TOSA), content specialists, peer teachers, etc.) for collaboration on activities,
taking developmental observations to a medical provider, or referral to an outside agency for
assessment and possible services with the creation of an Individualized Family Service Plan
(IFSP).

Center-based teachers will report each family’s choice of action to the Inclusion Content
Specialist, Health team members, Mental Health Specialist, and any other relevant support staff,
with the written permission of each family. The support staff will then begin to build
relationships with collaborating agencies, including but not limited to Alta California Regional
Center, Sacramento County Office of Education, and Elica Health Services. Families will
determine what type of information sharing will be implemented using written consent and
transition meetings. The collaborating agencies will offer many services within the family home
or another community environment. Services may be provided within the center-based setting
when this arrangement is in the child's best interests. Consultation and coaching for teaching
staff will be provided by the coordinating agency and the Inclusion Content Specialist as
needed. All relevant documentation of services, goals, etc., will be kept separate from general
child portfolios, with confidentiality protocols in place at all times.

Children transitioning from home-based to our center-based EHS locations will be provided an
individual timeline of enrollment to maintain consistency for the family, increase their access to
individualized education, and allow maximum attention to the identification of the Least
Restrictive Environment (LRE) based on their level of needed support. Children transitioning
from our center-based EHS programs into an HS classroom will be similarly placed. Families
will meet with their transition team (Current teacher(s), case manager from their service
provider, appropriate support staff, and assigned HS classroom teacher when possible) to
address the timeline for continued services, needed assessments, adjusted goals, and tentative
start date. All children with IFSPs will be transitioned and enrolled based on their individual
needs and LRE determination, with attention placed upon family input, preference, and need.

When children currently enrolled in EHS programs are identified as needing developmental
support but do not qualify for an IFSP or comparable service arrangements, the Inclusion
Content Specialist, Mental Health Therapist, and TOSA will provide teaching staff with lesson
planning guidance, feedback on strategy documentation/implementation and family connections
with additional support (Family Engagement Content Specialist, School Community workers,
Family and Community Engagement team, etc.). As children transition from EHS to an HS
placement, the current teacher will provide all relevant documentation, strategies, and
observations to the HS teaching staff before the child’s start date. This will ensure a continuum
of care and support for the child’s success in their new environment.

Head Start-

SJUSD ECE inclusion preschool programs currently include 20 slots reserved for children
enrolling with affirmed IEPs containing specific goals for an inclusive environment with
additional paraeducator support. Each of the six identified classrooms has one general education
                                                                                                     70
                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
       teacher, one supporting special education teacher, one full-time Child-Development Assistant
       (CDA), and one full-day Instructional Aide (IA). These inclusion slots are reserved for students
       whose least restrictive environment has been documented as a general education classroom with
       a shared IA within the full-day program. This placement is included within the child’s current
       IEP.

       Children enrolled in a designated inclusion placement have mild to moderate needs, with
       modifications or accommodations that can be effectively met in a full-day, play-based
       environment. Educational categories may include, but are not limited to, autism spectrum
       disorder, speech delay, physical impairments, or other cognitive delays. The special education
       teacher and IA will be in the classroom to work with the inclusion students to meet their IEP
       goals and help build children’s school readiness skills. The additional staff will lower the
       teacher-child ratio in identified inclusion classrooms.

       Children enrolled in all SJUSD ECE classrooms are screened and monitored throughout the
       year for developmental and behavioral growth. During registration, a family member completes
       the Ages and Stages Questionnaires (ASQ 3 and ASQ 2 SE) to share their child’s current skills,
       with a notation of the strengths and concerns they observe. Physical exams are also required for
       each child, and their physician may note additional development information.

       Most services for preschool children are provided on-site during scheduled class time. Families
       may provide additional services off-site, or a student may attend a specialized program within
       the district. Children enrolled in multiple placements with an affirmed IEP will be provided
       transportation between services to provide minimum impact on family schedules and maximum
       access to all environments throughout the school day. In-classroom services are logged and
       submitted monthly to the Inclusion Content Specialist. The Monthly Special Education Update
       form is completed by the general education classroom teacher each month and then submitted to
       the Inclusion Content Specialist. This form lists children enrolled with IEPs, the referral
       process, and the outcome as screenings and assessments are performed. Off-site services are
       reported to the Inclusion Content Specialist on an “as needed” basis when the child’s general
       education program schedule does not align with their off-site schedule.

       If a child is identified as Does Not Qualify (DNQ) for services and goals or does not qualify to be
       screened for developmental needs under an educational category; in this case, the support staff will
       transition to alternate support for the child, family, and teaching staff. The Inclusion Content
       Specialist will consult with the Special Education Preschool team to offer the following options:
       implementing a 504 plan accommodating specific needs, coordinating family meetings to provide
       materials and strategies to bring school and home environments, facilitating the creation of a
       Behavior Support Plan (BSP), with the support of the Mental Health Therapist, to address specific
       challenges the child experiences in the classroom and working with the Health team to rule out
       medical impacts to a child’s success at home and in the school.

•   Describe how your program will ensure the individualized needs of children with disabilities are met,
    including how the program will collaborate with and help parents in the process and how the program
    will coordinate and collaborate with the local agency responsible for implementing IDEA.




                                                                                                              71
              SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                   CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                            2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)

Early Head Start-

During the registration and enrollment process, the health team and enrollment technicians will
review all paperwork submitted by families, communicating with the inclusion content specialist
when a child has been identified with a developmental concern. ASQ screening results will be
reviewed and discussed with the family at the first home visit, with a plan determined for the
following steps: observe and document until the next milestone screening, referral to a
collaborating agency, or referral for additional medical review. Children will be provided with
lesson planning tailored to their developmental profiles, with frequent documentation of
successful strategies, areas of continuing need, and activities offered to families to implement in
the home environment. Families will be provided with frequent opportunities for community
resources of support development, opportunities to review their child’s progress as needed, and
guidance in identifying interventions that best meet their needs.

Families moving through the developmental assessment process work closely with their home or
classroom teacher, School Community Worker, and other support staff as needed. Our Family and
Community Engagement Department collaborates with local advocacy and community support
agencies to support families as needed. At any time, our Mental Health Therapist is available for
family meetings, classroom observations, or consultation of support services. Children will remain
in their current placement and schedule, with individualized support, unless alternative supports
are requested and agreed to by the family during this process.

Family rights are reviewed during orientation for all EHS programs in SJUSD, specifically rights
relating to all collaborating Special Education and Mental Health Support Services. Families are
allowed to sign an observation permission form at enrollment/orientation, allowing support staff
to enter classrooms with the focus on supporting the entire enrolled group and the professional
development of the teaching team. Children will not be screened, assessed, provided individual
interventions, or removed from the daily routine of the classroom without the written
understanding and permission of the family.

Head Start-

San Juan Unified Special Education program managers and San Juan Unified ECE administrators,
TOSAs, and Inclusion Content Specialist meet bi-monthly to discuss needs within the designated
inclusion classrooms, discuss needs for supporting children enrolled within general education
classrooms who display developmental differences, and plan for professional development and
training needed for staff. All preschool general education teachers are invited to the IEP meetings
with written permission from the family. When teachers cannot attend after receiving the
invitation, they can give input through a feedback questionnaire on the child’s strengths and any
areas of concern within the classroom. The inclusion content specialist will attend all IEPs for
child, family, and classroom support. Teachers will individualize for all students within the
school, incorporating IEP goals, 504 accommodations, and specific developmental strategies as
needed per child. Documentation will be submitted to the Education and Inclusion Content
Specialists on a quarterly timeline and will be referenced in each child’s Desired Results
Developmental Profile online portfolio (DRDP). Parents will be offered four individual
opportunities to discuss their child’s development: two home visits and two family conferences.
The first home visit will share the ASQ 3 and ASQ 2 SE results from registration screening and
                                                                                                      72
            SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                 CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                          2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
review them by the classroom teacher. The second home visit will focus on transition in one of
three ways: re-enrolling with a Head Start classroom, enrolling in a Transitional Kindergarten
program (TK), or enrolling in a Kindergarten program. If a family remains within the district, each
child receives a digital articulation summary questionnaire that will be submitted to their next
classroom teacher. Children moving to a program outside SJUSD will receive their DRDP
portfolio documentation as a digital file for the family to use as needed.

Enrolled children can be referred for developmental screening when needed. The Speech and
Language Pathologists (SLPs) are available on each HS campus to receive screening referral
forms signed by families with the classroom teacher. Screenings are placed during the scheduled
classroom times and are logged on the Disability Services Log (DIS). If a child is identified as
having a delay in communication, the SLP will initiate a process of enrolling the child with San
Juan Unified Central Enrollment. Families will receive the screening results, a comprehensive
speech assessment referral, or a team-as-a-whole developmental assessment referral. A speech
assessment will focus on a child’s ability to engage in expressive and receptive communication
and is conducted by the site SLP, with additional SLP support staff as needed. An entire team
assessment may include a variety of SJUSD specialists: a Special Education Preschool teacher, an
Occupational Therapist, an Adaptive Physical Education teacher, a School Psychologist, etc.

With the family's agreement, the child is added to a tracking spreadsheet with the Central
Enrollment team. The SLP will work with the School Community workers and classroom teacher
to support the family in completing district enrollment. Families will submit proof of residence
within SJUSD, following district requirements, and will then be contacted by the Special
Education assessment coordinator to sign an assessment plan. Appropriate assessment timelines
are rigorously followed, and families are provided with frequent communication during the
process.

Families moving through the developmental assessment process work closely with their classroom
teacher, School Community worker, and other support staff as needed. The Family and
Community Engagement Department collaborates with local advocacy and community support
agencies to support families as needed. The Mental Health Therapist is available for family
meetings, classroom observations, or consultation of support services. Children will remain in
their current placement and schedule, with individualized support, unless alternative supports are
requested and agreed to by the family during this process.

Family rights are reviewed during orientation for all HS programs in SJUSD, specifically rights
relating to all Special Education and Mental Health Support Services. Families are allowed to sign an
observation permission form at enrollment/orientation, allowing support staff to enter classrooms
with the focus on supporting the entire enrolled group and the professional development of the
teaching team. Children will not be screened, assessed, provided individual interventions, or removed
from the daily routine of the classroom without the written understanding and permission of the
family.

NEW! Updated Performance Standard Requirements
  • 1302.41, 1302.42 (b), 1302.46 (b) Describe how the program consistently integrates mental health
     into all aspects of program service delivery.

       Mental health continues to be a high priority for San Juan Unified ECE and is integrated into all
       matters of inclusion practices. The MHT is always available to families needing emergency or
       general consultation. Learning that a child is not meeting regular milestones and may need to be
       assessed for special support or a diagnosis can be very stressful and challenging for a family.
       Throughout all the processes named above, the MHT is always front and center, either participating
       in parent meetings or completing one-on-one consultations with families in need.

       The families meet with multiple staff members when they start the enrollment process, and they are
       always looking for families in distress. If there are any signs of need from the family when they meet
       with the AFST to complete enrollment paperwork, the Credentialed School Nurse, School
       Community Worker, or support staff during screening all staff are prepared to provide resources.
       Teachers are aware of resources and can contact the School Community Worker or MHT if they need
       the family. Additionally, working closely with the SPED department gives families one more
       resource and support system to contact if needed.

       Social-emotional learning is also highly valued and shared with parents regularly, whether through
       parent–teacher conferences, parent meetings, policy committee meetings, or parent workshops. San
       Juan Unified ECE values the importance of early intervention and parent education.

11. Transitions (1302 Subpart G)

   Please address both center-based and home-based programs.

   •   Describe strategies and practices to support successful transitions in:
                     i. Transitions to and from Early Head Start;

       Transitions from EHS Home-Based to Center-Based: When an EHS slot in a center becomes
       available, the Home-Based students take priority. The Admissions and Family Services Technician
       (AFST) first checks the waitlists for any Home-based students. An additional contact to the home-
       based teachers serving families in that area is made to see if any families may not be on the waitlist
       but have shared an interest in putting their child in a center. If the child is ready, the Home-Based
       Teacher (HBT) works with the AFST and the Health Assistant (HA) to ensure all the paperwork has
       been completed. The SCW and, when possible, the Home-Based teacher attend the parent
       orientation led by the center-based teacher when all paperwork has been finalized and confirmed by
       the AFST. Additionally, the home-based teacher visits the child in the center to check how they are
       doing, and the SCW checks in with families to follow up on family needs and goals.

       Transitions from EHS-based, Home-Based, or Center-Based to HS Preschool: San Juan Unified
       continues to utilize the internal “Transition Plan to Preschool” with teachers and families to ensure
       that the parents understand the process and their options for care. The plan begins when students are
       30 months old, and families select the Head Start classroom of choice. They are added to the waitlist
       for that classroom 3 months before they turn 36 months. The Transition Plan is aligned with grantee
       policy and Head Start Program Performance Standards (HSPPS). It ensures that all efforts have been

                                                                                                                74
                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
    made to transfer EHS students into the HS program. If spots are open at other sites, families on
    waitlists are offered enrollment at the open site. If the first choice is unavailable, AFSTs, teachers,
    and families communicate to determine if other locations or programs will be acceptable to the
    families. When possible, the preschool teacher is notified of the transition to allow the preschool
    teacher to reach out to the family and previous teacher to help the transition run smoothly and learn as
    much as possible about the student and family. Additionally, if the child is transitioning from an EHS
    center-based program, all growth and progress documented on Learning Genie by the EHS center
    teacher is available to the preschool teacher.

               ii.     Transitions from Head Start to Kindergarten; and

    To ensure HS children have a smooth transition into kindergarten, the Education and Disabilities
    Content Specialists collaborate continuously with the Elementary Early Learning TOSAs. In addition
    to all the school readiness preparation done in the classroom, this ensures vital collaboration between
    preschool and kindergarten classrooms. Transition resources are updated and shared with teachers
    and families to prepare for the transition to kindergarten. School Community Workers also support
    families individually with any needs during the transition process. The May classroom parent meeting
    is focused on kindergarten transitions, and the May Policy Committee meeting also provides a
    presentation on best practices for parents preparing their children for kindergarten. Individualized
    Student Articulation Cards are created by preschool teachers and passed on to the TK teachers,
    kindergarten teachers, and elementary principals to inform them of the preschool student’s progress.

               iii.    Transitions between programs.

    San Juan Unified supports families transitioning into different programs by meeting with them and
    providing resources about transitioning enrollment and information about new programs they will be
    enrolling in. SCWs have resources available to share with families when they meet with them. San
    Juan Unified AFSTs and SCWs work collaboratively with SETA to make referrals, check space
    availability, and support the transition process.

    NEW! Updated Performance Standard Requirements
•   1302.41, 1302.42 (b), 1302.46 (b) Describe how the program consistently integrates mental health
    into all aspects of program service delivery

    As transitions can often be difficult for students and families, teachers and SCWs always provide the
    contact information of the MHT in the program as a resource.

                  SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                       CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS

12. Services to Enrolled Pregnant Women (1302 Subpart H)

FOR EHS PROGRAMS ONLY

  •   Describe how the program facilitates access to a source of ongoing care for enrolled pregnant women
      who do not have existing access to such care.

      The program emphasizes the importance of ensuring that mothers, fathers, partners, and other key
      family members can access healthcare providers and receive assistance obtaining healthcare services.
      Pregnant women enrolled in the San Juan Unified Early Head Start Home-Based Program are
      informed by their Home-Based Teachers (HBTs) and health staff about available healthcare services,
      community resources, and relevant events. If they lack access to care, the HBT, in collaboration with
      the Credentialed School Nurse and School Community Workers, provides resources and follow-up
      until a primary healthcare provider is established. The Credentialed School Nurse reviews prenatal
      history, conducts nutrition screenings for pregnant or lactating women, provides post-delivery
      support, and refers families to community service agencies as needed.

      NEW! Updated Performance Standard Requirements
  •   1302.80 (d) Describe how newborn visits are provided or offered and the topics discussed during the
      visits. At a minimum, newborn visits must include maternal mental and physical health, safe sleep,
      infant health, and support for basic needs.

      Home visitors use the Parents as Teachers (PAT) and Partners for Healthy Babies (PFHB)
      Curriculum to assess the mother’s physical recovery from childbirth and screen for postpartum
      depression. They provide support and resources to address any mental health concerns. Home visitors
      use PAT and Partners for Healthy Babies to educate parents on safe sleep practices, such as placing
      the baby on their back to sleep, using a firm mattress, and keeping the sleep area free of soft bedding
      and toys. The baby’s growth and development are monitored, and parents receive guidance on
      feeding, recognizing developmental milestones, and addressing health concerns. The HBT provides
      resources and referrals to help families meet basic needs like food, housing, and healthcare. (WIC,
      local Food banks)

  • 1302.80 (e) Describe how the program tracks and records services received by the enrolled
  pregnant woman or pregnant person, both from the program and referrals to community agencies.

      Home visitors use a post-delivery form to record the topics they addressed during the visits with the
      pregnant mom. The same information is recorded under PIR in Child Plus and shared with the nurses.
      Health issues and needs are assessed at enrollment by utilizing the Prenatal History Form.

  •   1302.80 (f) Describe how the program helps address disparities in maternal and birth outcomes across
      racial and ethnic groups.

      Home visitors collaborate with local community organizations to provide families access to culturally
      relevant resources and support services. This includes partnerships with healthcare providers, social
      services, and community groups focusing on minority populations. For example, they provide info

                                                                                                                76
                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
    about Black Mothers United. This is a program that provides education, resources, and support to
    pregnant African American women residing in Sacramento County to help ensure a smooth and safe
    pregnancy and a healthy baby. La Familia Counseling Center provides multicultural counseling,
    youth services, and family support to the Latino community. Asian Resources, INC. offers
    employment, education, and social services to the Asian and Pacific Islander communities. Home
    visitors help Muslim moms find appropriate prenatal vitamins without gelatin or pork to ensure they
    receive the necessary nutrients while adhering to their dietary restrictions.

•   1302.81 Describe how the program ensures the required prenatal and postpartum information,
    education, and services are provided to enrolled pregnant women, mothers, fathers, partners, or other
    family members.

    Home visitors document each visit weekly on a home visit plan, including the topics discussed,
    assessments made, and any referrals provided. This information is recorded in a secure database to
    track the family’s progress and ensure continuity of care. Home visitors use the Edinburgh Postnatal
    Depression Scale (EPDS) to help identify mothers experiencing postpartum depression and refer
    them to appropriate services. This usually happens after the newborn reaches 2 months.

•    1302.82(a) What is the curriculum used in serving pregnant women? Describe the curriculum and
    how it includes the provision of services to pregnant women and pregnant people, it should be a
    maternal health curriculum to support prenatal and postpartum education needs including other
    relevant family members, and support the transition process.

    The home visitors use the PAT and PFHB curricula. Each curriculum is described below:
     Parents as Teachers (PAT):
    • With the PAT curriculum, home visitors assess the mother’s physical recovery from childbirth
       and also screen for postpartum depression. They provide support and resources to address any
       mental health concerns.
    • Home visitors educate parents on safe sleep practices, such as placing the baby on their back to
       sleep, using a firm mattress, and keeping the sleep area free of soft bedding and toys.
    • The baby’s growth and development are monitored, and parents receive guidance on feeding,
       recognizing developmental milestones, and addressing health concerns.
    • PAT provides resources and referrals to help families meet basic needs like food, housing, and
       healthcare.

    Partners for a Healthy Baby (PFHB):
    • This program also focuses on the mother’s well-being, including physical recovery and mental
       health. Home visitors discuss postpartum depression and provide resources for support.
    • The curriculum includes detailed information on safe sleep practices to prevent SIDS,
       emphasizing the importance of a safe sleep environment.
    • Home visitors track the baby’s growth, offer feeding support, and ensure the baby is meeting
       developmental milestones. They also provide information on immunizations and regular health
       check-ups.
    • The program offers extensive resources and referrals to assist families with basic needs, ensuring
       they can access necessary services and support.


                                                                                                            77
            SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                 CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                          2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
Both curricula emphasize the importance of thorough documentation to monitor the effectiveness of
the support provided and to make necessary adjustments to meet the family’s needs. They both
provide information on the stages of fetal growth and development, including the importance of
nutrition and avoiding harmful substances like alcohol, drugs, and tobacco. PAT and PFHB educate
expecting mothers on what to expect during labor and delivery, pain management options, and
creating a birth plan.

Home visitors encourage the involvement of partners, fathers, and other family members in prenatal
and postpartum care to create a supportive environment.

                   SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                        CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS

Section B – Governance, Organizational, and Management Structures

Governance Structure (45 CFR Part 1301 and Section 642(c)-(d) in the Act):

Provide updates on the following areas. If changes were made, describe the rationale for the changes such as
new data from an updated community assessment, ongoing oversight or from using data for continuous
improvement as described in 1302.102(b)-(c). If no updates or changes have occurred, include a sentence to
that effect. Where applicable, describe any challenges in these areas and how the program is working to
address those challenges.

1. Governance (1301.2(b)(2) and 1301.3(c)(2))

Governing Body and Policy Council

   •   Describe if there are changes in the Board or Governing Body and Policy Council membership.

       Since March 2024, two board members have termed out, and new ones have been voted in. The board
       members are Ben Avey, Tanya Kravchuk, Manuel Perez, Zima Creason, Nick Bloise, Abid
       Stanekzai, and Pam Costa.

   •   Describe how the governing body and the policy council receive key program information as outlined
       in 1301.2(b)(2) to inform their ongoing responsibilities including how decisions submitted by the
       policy council are incorporated into the decision-making process.
           ➢ Describe the process for communication with the governing board and policy council.

           San Juan Unified is a delegate agency of SETA and has a policy committee instead of a policy
           council. In addition, the School Board that oversees San Juan Unified LEA is also the governing
           board of the San Juan Unified Head Start program. Policy committee monthly meetings are made
           up of parent representatives from each classroom in the Head Start Program. One representative is
           elected as the Chair of the policy committee. A secretary, Co-chair, treasurer, and parliamentarian
           are also elected and become the executive committee. The executive committee meets the week
           before the policy committee meeting to approve the agenda and review attendance and previous
           meeting minutes. Once approved, an agenda packet is sent to all policy committee members the
           week before the meeting. The packet contains the agenda, prior meeting minutes, informational
           items, fiscal reports, enrollment reports, content reports, and parent resources. Policy committee
           members review the agenda packet before the monthly meeting. During the meeting, members
           discuss and vote on action items, listen to program reports and various informational
           presentations, and have many opportunities for feedback and questions about the program.

           After the policy committee meeting is adjourned, a policy committee meeting packet is made for
           each School Board member. The packets are sent to the School Board office on the same day as
           the policy committee meeting, so there is no time lapse in the information received. Each School
           Board member packet contains the agenda, the approved minutes from the previous month, fiscal
           reports, enrollment reports, content reports, and the current month’s agenda. As a result of
           receiving these packets, the school board is always up to date on any program changes or updates
           throughout the school year. The program manager also attends regular school board meetings and

                                                                                                                 79
                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
       is available to answer questions the school board may have about any board items related to Head
       Start.

•   Describe other key processes to ensure the governing body maintains effective ongoing oversight of
    program operations and accountability for federal funds.
       ➢ Describe training and technical assistance or orientation sessions for the governing body,
           advisory committee members, and the policy council.

           Once a year, Head Start Policy committee members and governing body members receive
           orientation training in various methods. In-person training is provided to the new
           representatives, and for those needing a virtual option, a Zoom meeting is provided. Training
           materials are either provided in person or emailed for the Zoom. A welcome packet, which
           includes information on the orientation training, is also given to all incoming policy
           committee members. Additionally, refresher trainings are provided as needed throughout the
           year if new members continue to join after the orientation training opportunity is provided.
           This is unnecessary for the School Board as minimal turnover occurs among the board
           members.

       ➢ Include examples of the governing body and policy council using key program information to
         conduct its responsibilities.

           The monthly reports inform the Governing Body and Policy Committee's decisions regarding
           various budget items and the yearly grant application.

       ➢ Include examples of parent committees informing program policies, activities, and services.

           When program changes are being considered, the program design committee meets and
           reviews the program changes to offer feedback and perspective from the parent community.
           The parents from the program design committee shared with the policy committee what was
           discussed at the program design meeting. Input is considered, and the administration works to
           include parent needs in all program design decisions. Policy committee members also support
           the program by taking the yearly parent satisfaction survey before it is sent out. This allows
           the program to get feedback on the survey tool before distributing the survey to all parents.
           Input from all parent surveys is considered for program decisions. One example of a
           continuous request from parents is to increase surveys. During policy committee meetings, the
           number of EHS slots was growing. Based on this request, changes were made for the 24-25
           school year to expand the toddler programs. Also, in the new business section of the policy
           committee meeting, parents bring forward concerns that they would like more information.
           These concerns are then created as items for follow-up on the agenda for the next meeting.
           Reoccurring topics that have come up have been nutrition, field trips, and enrollment efforts.
           As a result, the head of the nutritional services department presented at a Policy Committee
           meeting and addressed the questions and concerns of the policy committee members. Parents
           also have the choice to serve on hiring panels and help choose the best candidates for various
           positions in Head Start and Early Head Start. Finally, drafts of the self-assessment document
           and the five-year goals for the program are shared with the policy committee meeting to
           provide additional revisions, feedback, and suggestions on priorities before the grant is
           submitted.

                   SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                        CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                                 2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)

2. Human Resources Management (1302 Subpart I)

   •   Describe if there are changes in Head Start Director and other key leadership positions.

   •   Provide an organizational chart identifying the management and staffing structure, including the

       responsibility and lines of communication.

       See the Organizational Chart Provided

   •   Describe systems developed to ensure criminal background checks occur before hiring for all staff,
       consultants, and contractors in the program.

       All staff hired in the San Juan Unified School District must complete a full fingerprint and
       background check. The new employee's start date is not given until the background check is complete
       and documented.

   NEW! Updated Performance Standard Requirements
   • 1302.91(e)(8)(ii) Mental Health Consultants' Licensure. Describe how the program will comply with
     the requirements related to this regulation: A program must ensure all mental health consultants are
     licensed or under the supervision of licensed mental health professionals. Programs also must use
     mental health consultants with knowledge of and experience in serving young children and their
     families.

       San Juan Unified ECE is committed to ensuring compliance with 1302.91(e)(8)(ii) by working with
       mental health consultants who are either fully licensed or working under the supervision of a licensed
       mental health professional. Establishing partnerships with credentialed mental health providers who
       have specialized knowledge and experience in early childhood development, trauma-informed care,
       and family-centered support is essential to the program. San Juan Unified ECE verifies all
       consultants' credentials and supervisory arrangements to ensure adherence to licensing requirements.
       Additionally, ongoing professional development opportunities are provided to enhance consultants’
       expertise in serving young children and their families, ensuring responsive and developmentally
       appropriate mental health support.

   •   1302.92(b)(1) Professional Development Plans - Describe how the program will comply with the
       requirements related to this regulation: Programs must develop professional development plans for
       full-time staff providing direct services to children, as required in Section 648A(f) of the Head Start
       Act.


                                                                                                                 81
                SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                     CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                              2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
    San Juan Unified will ensure compliance with 1302.92(b)(1) by developing professional development
    plans for all staff providing direct services to children. These plans are created in collaboration with
    leadership teams and administration, aligning with the requirements outlined in Section 648A(f) of
    the Head Start Act. Each plan will include ongoing training in child development, effective teaching
    practices, family engagement, and trauma-informed care. Access is provided to workshops, coaching,
    and credentialing programs, such as the Child Development Associate (CDA) credential, to support
    staff in meeting professional standards. Regular staff surveys and feedback will ensure continuous
    growth, improving the quality of care and education for the children and families we serve. Data from
    DRDPs will determine the developmental areas where staff training can be provided.

•   1302.92(b)(2–3) Annual Training - Describe how the program will comply with the requirements
    related to this regulation: Programs must ensure staff receive annual training on
    o Mandatory reporting
    o Positive strategies to understand and support children’s social and emotional development
    o The knowledge, experience, and competencies to improve child and family outcomes

    San Juan Unified ensures compliance with 1302.92(b)(2–3) by providing annual comprehensive
    training for all staff on mandatory reporting, positive strategies for supporting children’s social and
    emotional development, and the knowledge, experience, and competencies needed to improve child
    and family outcomes. Staff participate in mandatory child abuse and neglect reporting training to
    understand legal responsibilities and best practices for identifying and responding to concerns.
    Additionally, professional development on social-emotional learning (SEL) strategies, trauma-
    informed care, and positive behavior support will be offered to foster children’s emotional well-
    being. Training will include best practices in family engagement, responsive teaching strategies, and
    developmental assessments to enhance outcomes for children and families. Training sessions will be
    evidence-based, facilitated by experts, and include hands-on learning to ensure staff apply their
    knowledge effectively in daily interactions with children and families.

•   1302.93(d) Culture of Wellness - Describe how the program will comply with the requirements
    related to this regulation: A program should cultivate a program-wide culture of wellness that
    empowers staff as professionals and supports staff to effectively accomplish their job responsibilities
    in a high-quality manner.

    San Juan Unified is committed to fostering a program-wide culture of wellness that empowers staff
    and supports their ability to provide high-quality services. Wellness initiatives that address physical,
    mental, and emotional well-being, including access to employee assistance programs (EAPs), stress
    management workshops, and mindfulness training, will be implemented. Staff will receive regular
    opportunities for peer support, reflective supervision, and professional coaching to help navigate
    workplace challenges. San Juan Unified ECE promotes a healthy work-life balance by offering
    flexible scheduling, incentives or prizes for active engagement, and recognizing staff achievements.
    By creating a supportive, inclusive, and wellness-focused environment, San Juan Unified will
    enhance staff satisfaction, retention, and effectiveness in serving children and families.

                                                                                                               82
                   SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                        CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                                 2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
   •   1302.101(a)(2) Employee Engagement - Describe how the program will comply with the
       requirements related to this regulation: A program must comply with enhanced requirements for
       employee engagement to promote more responsive management styles designed to identify and
       resolve barriers to high-quality job performance.

       San Juan Unified ECE offers all staff clear and reasonable roles and responsibilities through
       onboarding and ongoing training throughout the year. Feedback surveys are utilized to evaluate
       understanding and also feedback from staff on their responsibilities and what support they need.
       Monthly site staff meetings also seek input from staff about what support is necessary for them to
       succeed in their role. Barriers are often identified at these meetings and also through staff feedback
       forms. If coaches and leadership can problem-solve obstacles, then various solutions can be offered to
       the staff. If some barriers arise from external issues outside of ECE, then staff members are
       encouraged to bring it forward to their union representative.

3. Program Management and Quality Improvement (see 1302 Subpart J)

   •   Does the agency have a pending Corrective Action Plan (CAP) from SETA (for example, under-
       enrollment, health and safety/supervision)? If yes, describe the status and progress in meeting the
       corrective action requirements. Describe the ongoing oversight and new procedures that prevent the
       recurrence of previous quality and compliance issues, including previously identified non-
       compliances/deficiencies, safety incidents, and audit findings.

       In the Summer of 2024, the Home-Based program was evaluated by SETA. All Corrective Action
       Items from that monitoring process have been closed and completed. SETA conducted a Health and
       Safety Screening in the Fall of 2025. All Corrective Action Items for that monitoring process have
       identified Immediate and Long-Term Corrective Actions. All Immediate items have been closed out
       and completed as of January 15th. All long-term corrective actions will be written into the grant
       monitoring plan.

   •   Describe continuous program improvement activities and how the program uses collected data in
       enrollment, attendance, health and nutrition, safety, and supervision to change program practices.

       The Head Start Grant cycle allows us to continue to review data, make program improvement plans,
       and complete yearly evaluations. State Grants and Nutrition Grants also provide structure for
       continuous monitoring and program improvement. After the policy committee approves the grant, the
       school board approves the grant funding in April, and the program area plan is completed based on
       the goals and plans made in the approved grant for the upcoming school year. The content specialists
       begin preparation of their specific areas of the plan and develop implementation strategies for the
       upcoming school year. During the summer, content specialists and TOSAs develop the theme and
       focus of the August pre-service program and create resources that the staff and classroom staff can
       use throughout the school year. The leadership team is collaboratively involved in planning the
       teaching staff's professional development experiences. Training at the beginning of the year strongly
       focuses on safety and supervision to ensure all teachers understand the most critical aspect of their

                                                                                                                83
               SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                    CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                             2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
   job in the classroom. A safety checklist evaluates the classroom teacher’s knowledge of all the safety
   procedures in the classroom and must be sent in by September. This is followed up with individual
   coaching from TOSAs and is provided to teachers needing more support and additional training.

   Content specialists begin the self-assessment process in November. Training and resources are given
   for the program goals, and appropriate data is chosen and analyzed to evaluate program growth.
   Strengths and Areas of Growth are established with action items. Monitoring tools are utilized
   regularly, providing the data needed for the self-assessment process. Action plans are developed from
   identified growth areas to allow the program to continue in its direction or intentionally pivot to get
   back on track.

NEW! Updated Performance Standard Requirements
• 1302.101(a)(5), 1302.102(d) Training on Incident Reporting- Describe the agency’s internal reporting
  procedure on health and safety incidents (from the classroom level to administration level to Grantee)
  to ensure it meets the Grantee’s reporting timeline.

   San Juan Unified Health and Safety Incident Reporting Training Plan

   Objective

   This training plan establishes a clear and systematic internal reporting procedure for health and safety
   incidents occurring in all San Juan Unified classrooms. The process ensures compliance with federal
   regulations and timely communication from the classroom level to the administration and governing
   bodies.

   Training Overview
   Participants:

   •   Classroom Staff (Teachers, Child Development Assistants, Non-Instructional Support Aides)
   •   Site Supervisors/Center Directors
   •   Health and Safety Coordinators
   •   Program Administrators
   •   Governing Body and Policy Council

   Training Schedule:

   •   Initial training upon hire
   •   Bi-annual refresher training
   •   Additional training as necessary following incidents or policy updates

   Training Methods:

   •   In-person workshops
   •   Online training modules on Public Works
   •   Case study analysis
   •   Role-playing exercises
   •   Q&A sessions

   Incident Reporting Procedure

                                                                                                              84
            SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                 CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                          2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
Step 1: Immediate Response at Classroom Level

Responsible: Classroom Staff

•   Ensure the safety and well-being of all children and staff.
•   Administer first aid or seek medical assistance if necessary.
•   Notify the Site Supervisor/Center Director immediately.
•   Document the incident using the Internal Incident Report Form.
•   If the incident involves suspected child abuse, immediately report to Child Protective Services as
    required by law.

Step 2: Administrator Review

Responsible: Program Administrator

•   Review the incident report within 24 hours.
•   Conduct an initial investigation and gather witness statements if applicable.
•   Determine if external reporting is required (e.g., child protective services, law enforcement, or
    licensing bodies).

Step 3: Health and Safety Assessment

Responsible: Program Administrator

•   Evaluate the severity and implications of the incident.
•   Determine whether the incident falls under the federal reporting requirements.
•   If the incident qualifies, escalate to the Program Manager within 48 hours.
•   Guide corrective actions and preventive measures.

Step 4: Program Manager, Upper Management, and Governing Body Notification

Responsible: Program Manager

•   Report significant incidents to the responsible HHS official within seven calendar days if required
    under regulation §1302.102(d)(1)(ii).
•   Ensure that incidents requiring notification to state, tribal, or local authorities are appropriately
    reported.
•   Oversee the development and implementation of corrective action plans, if applicable.

Step 5: Documentation and Compliance Review

Responsible: Program Manager

•   Maintain comprehensive records of all incidents and reports.
•   Publish and disseminate an annual report per §1302.102(d)(2).
•   Ensure compliance with all federal, state, and local reporting requirements.
•   Submit a quality improvement plan if a deficiency is identified.



                                                                                                            85
                     SACRAMENTO COUNTY HEAD START / EARLY HEAD START
                          CONTINUING APPLICATION REQUIREMENTS
                                   2025-2026 (YEAR 2 of 5)
       Key Reporting Requirements

       All incidents must be reported immediately and documented thoroughly. The following types of
       incidents require mandatory reporting:

       •     Significant health or safety incidents affecting a child in a Head Start-funded setting.
       •     Financial viability threats, data breaches, or legal proceedings involving the program.
       •     Violations of child abuse and neglect laws, including those involving staff or volunteers.
       •     Classroom or center closures due to health or safety concerns.
       •     Conditions requiring reporting under §1304.12 (e.g., CACFP disqualification, licensing issues).
       •     Suspected maltreatment or endangerment by program personnel.
       •     Serious harm or injury caused by lack of maintenance or supervision.
       •     Unauthorized release of a child.

       Evaluation and Continuous Improvement

       •     Post-training assessments to gauge staff understanding.
       •     Regular audits of incident reports to ensure compliance.
       •     Collect feedback from staff and administration for process improvement.
       •     Updates to the training plan based on new regulations or identified deficiencies.

       This training plan ensures that San Juan Unified is equipped to handle and report incidents
       effectively, safeguarding the well-being of children and maintaining compliance with all federal and
       local regulations. San Juan Unified has an internal incident reporting system with IRIS that will
       report to Safe Schools to support each individual situation.
